Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two needles be by degrees in one place according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then treat the eye by pulling those veins gently, and suck out the blood every hour afterwards, until you see those veins being removed from the eye; and be careful not to touch the eye with the points of your spatulae, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss any of those veins; and when you have done that, make some green and red juice drop into the eye to corrupt what remains in the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to treat all of this in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains have subsided and you are assured that the abscess is hot, then start again in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems we've reached the end of a medieval medical text discussing eye treatments. The title "de la fistule de l'oil" translates to "of the fistula of the eye". A fistula is an abnormal connection or passageway between two normally separate body parts, and in this case, it's likely referring to a chronic infection or abscess affecting the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor's instruments are called "arissati" fistules: when you cure it with fire and a hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you must make an incision on the abscess where it should die, and extract all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument by which this shape is made; and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron to a pointy tip, and be sharpened like a file as much as in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is reduced; and do this as many times, then restore the place with medicated poultices.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is healed, and flesh has grown, and the core of the abscess has healed, and remains like that for 40 days, and it does not worsen and is not inflamed, and no bad accident happens to it, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other cause but to bring back the fistula to its original place according to this form: and that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and with hot medicines, and when it has been uncovered take one stick according to this form, and it should have an iron tip at three angles, and the shaft be thinned out until the point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the bone next to the abscess, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire stick until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what the blood flows in if they hold their hand over the wound; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the spot, the matter will come to the wound; which is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the pus of the wound
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the pus has completely drained from the wound and there is no further disturbance or decrease in size, it is necessary to tie up the patient; then clean the wound, then apply leeches with iron needles to suck, then put a poultice made of aloe, incense, and sarcocolle on top of the wound; then strain the wound by wrapping it with bandages and cloths; and the way to do this is to take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to how much pus the wound needs to be drained; then strain from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the leeches to suck without causing further injury; then remove the leeches and leave the wound strained day and night; and if you see the poultice become wet, it is necessary to tighten it more; then remove the poultice after the next day and night; and if you see the wound recovering, it is good; if not, then repeat the poulticing and bandaging and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the rupture of a membrane or skin ( possibly referring to a specific medical condition)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the membrane (toile uvee) ruptures and bursts open, and comes out in pieces like a grain of resin, and it's terrifying to see; then if you see it covering, the treatment is such that you insert an needle into the root of the lower part up to the top, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the wound; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle in place; then cut the thread and tie one part of the membrane around, and tighten it well, then extract the needle and put a piece of linen moistened with egg on top of the wound; and let it be until the thread sticks to the membrane, then dress the wound with comforting things until the pain is healed; and at any time the wound is restrained by the membrane each part in a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus appears in a great abundance, then make it pierce with a fine needle that comes from the center of the eye, and drain the moistened albuginum (a part of the eye) and descend into the pus, and enter inside as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the cornea of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not anything other than the cornea of the eye being assembled together, resembling a thread descending, and it's not a thread; and the way to appear in its treatment is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight chair, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and move them back and forth until you see the cornea come up to your eyes; then put it back in place, and do not let it descend or get dislodged, and shine light into it, and have the patient look at things as they normally would; and if it doesn't go down, know that it's a thread, and if the descending of the cornea is not prepared as we said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine needle and sew on the corneal membrane one point by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the cornea comes out; and when it's come out, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or hot water and fenugreek is boiled and mixed with honey, then be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the tears of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of water in the division, and what is needed to pierce; so work according to health. It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, out of the light for the sun, and hold their good eye and strain it very much; then place the paper on the eye in your left hand if the eye is left-handed, or in your right hand if the eye is right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right-handed; then place the point of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a nail in the white part of the eye to the smaller tear sac, then insert the instrument called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand so that it pierces in the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes into the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument just to the point where the water is, then press beneath one path after another. If the water now descends, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Il semble que nous ayons affaire à une traduction médiévale d'un texte scientifique ou médical, probablement un traité sur l'anatomie ou la chirurgie de l'œil. Voici ma traduction :
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are very hard, then you must take the instrument that is called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce the conjunctiva only slightly, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put alum in it, as we said; and when you finish this task, arrange for the patient to sleep on his back in a dark place; and be sure of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head nor to the right nor to the left, and keep him tied according to his condition until the third day; then untie him in the same dark house, and examine his eye, and make it see some things, and then put the tie back on until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but rather delay it, because the liquid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess forms, then untie the eye in front of the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the abscess; and when it is calm, then untie the eyelid and put a patch over his face to cover it for some days, and be sure to keep him in that dark house. And then slowly leave the house little by little, and return to his usual state; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iarach (a place in medieval times), who said that in his peaceful land they used to make alum incisions, through which the liquid would come out, but somehow I never saw anyone do it in our territory, nor did I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alum (algarde), because those who do not know them see them; and they are made of pure silver (or more likely, white lead or some other metal)
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads be of the same subtle appearance, and their ends in three sharp points (or corners).
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel (area)
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes different kinds of flesh bumps appear on the navel area, some of which resemble scorpions in shape. If they are of this kind, if they have a flesh bump with mixed colors (likely meaning a mix of red and white or other colors), and if they have a soft flesh bump of good color. In that case, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and pour some oil on them, and treat those bumps to dry them out; then take what you can hold in the subtle sharp edge of a spatula, as much as you know that flesh bump is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that you can't remove, then open it up completely with the sharp instruments (likely meaning scalpels or forceps), so that nothing is left; and if it's not swollen, or an abscess forms, then cut out the scab as needed; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize them until the swelling subsides and all the flesh bumps are removed; then pour oil on the navel area and drink water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the navel area opens up and moistors comes out as far as the palate, know that it is healed; and if moistors does not drain properly, know that there is flesh accumulating in the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut through: then it is necessary to insert a thread of linen, about the size of a finger, well oiled with hands, with a space of about an inch or less between each knot; and place the patient's nose on one end of the thread, and guide it so that it comes out through the mouth; and do this many times as children in school learn to do it, which is a simple thing for anyone who wants to try it. Then take the head that emerges from the navel area with one hand, and the other head that emerges from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart carefully so that the thread does not break; do this until you know that the knots have corroded the remaining flesh; then pull out the thread, clean it by rinsing it in water, and insert it back into the navel area as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all the remaining flesh; and then place a linen pad on the navel area for some days until it is healed, and if necessary, use dried medicines; and that's the form of the instrument to purify the head, with which one distills oils and medicines through the navel.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or white metal, resembling an open lamp or candle holder, with a handle; and it conducts heat to the same area. And if you see that [the navel area] is closed, then make a closed candle holder, and have the instruments full of oil to purify the head; and have one hand to hold the instrument when heating the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the skin
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	The shoulder often becomes diseased and grows so large that it can be seen, and it must be operated on at the beginning, removing all of its flesh. Then apply a cauter or burning medicine to it; and if you delay surgery until it is large, be aware if it has become hardened, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure substance, not of bad color, and you can see that you can completely remove it, the patient will feel empty and safe, and the wound will heal quickly and tightly.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the flesh is cut out
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous parts, it benefits little, in some men. Therefore, when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh and all its blood; and then sew the two lips together with a suture, and cure until it is healed; and if the lips have already dried out from one part and another, you should scrape off all parts of their crust as long as they are healing, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, and hold them in place, and sprinkle powdered blood of dragon on top of powdered incense, and put on top of the powders a piece of adhesive plaster or other sticking plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of stitching is that you assemble the cut: with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I told you earlier.
des apostemes des levres	Les apôtèmes des lèvres se présentent souvent sous la forme de tumeurs ou de bourgeons qui poussent sur les lèvres, en particulier après une blessure ou une irritation. Ils peuvent être douloureux et peut même gêner la fermeture des lèvres.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A multitude of people have a hard abscess inside the lips, similar to grains of millet, and smaller and larger ones. Then you must turn back the lips, and split them in each part, and take it as tweezers and press into each part; then fill the place after the vitriol incision, so that the blood is stopped; and then remove the scab, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the skin of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there appears on the gums a swollen skin, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, and cut at its root, and let it bleed or dry; then put on the place vitriol paste, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that skin returns after the incision, and appears many times, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are times when they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and there are times when the tooth is black and green and worm-eaten, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks. Then it is necessary for you to sit the ailing person in your hands, and their feet should be in your sanctuary, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, as long as there remains nothing; and do the same with the blackness and greenishness, and the yellowness and other blemishes, until they are cleansed. And if you take out what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to the work that the instrument shows, because the rasor with which one removes the teeth outside has other forms than those with which one removes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can to extract it, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, so that there should be no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is convinced that it must be extracted, you should make sure of the tooth's position. Many times, pain will deceive the patient, and they think it is a healthy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled; but the pain does not depart in any way, until the bad tooth is removed, because we have already wanted to do this for these saints; and when you are well convinced of the tooth's position, you should scrape around the tooth all around, with a spatula very sharp to protect the gum from all sides. Then move it to your thumbs or fine tweezers at the first notch and notch, until it is well loosened, then grasp the tweezers tightly; and the patient's foot should be in your sanctuary between their legs, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After, extract the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it doesn't come out easily, take one of these instruments and push it into each side gently, and then remove it as you did at first. And if the tooth is perforated or cracked, you should fill it with a plug, where the holes are; and if the instrument slips off the tweezers when extracting, make sure that it doesn't break when straining; and you must work very carefully around the gum to uncover the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be very careful not to break it and leave a part of it behind, and instruct the patient that the root will grow back into greater pain than before. Be careful not to do as foolish surgeons do, who through their haste and recklessness break the wheel sometimes, and do not bring what we have said; but sometimes bring great sickness from the roots that remain, or because they break the wheel, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with vinegar or oil of asafoetida and soap; and if bleeding comes from it, which happens often, apply the place with vitriol broth; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one must draw out the tooth first, should be long-pointed and have large handles, so that they do not double back when you pull on the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have thick handles so that they do not bend when being pulled, and be well-made of iron and have teeth to hold the wire.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the extraction site, you should put a wet cotton ball on the place in butter for a day or two, until the area is softened. Then insert the pincers called "algefri", with which the gums seem like the beak of a vulture; and they should be made inside as well as a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all the pincers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", which is to say a palinche (a type of drill or burr), whose shape is this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good. If not, you should help with all the instruments, whose shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one needs help from this instrument which has two handles, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fasteners that are in front in proportion to the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pincers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be for breaking, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise and subtle masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases in which the ancients did not teach a single instrument due to the diversity of cases, and one does not break the bone or other bones, unless they look for instruments as I have said, and help from gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding for holding the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of medicine suitable to this case, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then reap everything with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape, and its form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then scrape it. And if it is crowded with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the shape, and it resembles a small beak, and it should be made of iron with a sharp tip on top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file is rough and rough in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you cannot move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, take a file of this kind, of which this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also how one makes needles; and in sharpening the point of a tooth, one does so gradually, little by little, so that it does not move until it becomes sharp; then the plane smooths it at the end to be completely flat, and if the teeth are too sharp and they wound the tongue, one must hone the roughness so that it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front tooth rots through being hit or falling, and the patient cannot close their mouth over what they are eating without wincing, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but that is of no use; so one must restrain it with a thread of gold, because the silver wire turns green and rotten, but the gold does not change at all; and let the middle thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth turning, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the sick teeth, as many as there are, until you can do so skillfully up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then reapply the covering up to the part where you started, and draw your hand skillfully and gently, until it no longer moves; and let your loop be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then clip the ends of the thread with tweezers, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy tooth and the sick one, and place it in such a way that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens or breaks, re-tighten it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy ones and the two sick ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one must put it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and let nobody who is not wise and patient interfere with it; and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from an ox's rib, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it just as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to clip the thread to the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this growth comes from under the tongue or nature, when it is born thus; or by accident of a sutured wound; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous cord with great force, so that the tongue is disengaged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to a sutured wound, so insert an iron and cut with great force that ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is under; and when you have done this, then raise the head of the patient with rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then put over the tongue a linen cloth; and swab the patient every night, so that the wound does not close.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is green or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards the navel, and there is moisture, make an incision, and the lance it, and make a fine spatula, and deliver it from one part and from another; and if the pus goes to your work, put vinegar powder on top until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have removed all the fluid; then lift the abscess with oil and silk, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Never once comes from within the throat pouches which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard swelling of small sense and green color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron either for its bleeding; but leave it until it dies, and then you will cut it, or it would break on its own; and if it is white in color again, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cauterize, but first look if the swelling chills down and is soothed. Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his dogs should be in your sight, and open the mouth and take the forceps between his hands, and press the tongue under all the instrument, of which this is the shape; and it may be thin silver or thin lead just like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the swelling, then take the forceps and stick it into the almond, and pull it out above as far as you can; and remove any threads with it, then cauterize at the instrument, of which this is the shape, which looks like a hook; and although the end is curved, one place to another, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument handy, then cauterize with pincers, of which this shape is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be cut on one side, and on the other named; and when you have cut out one of the almonds, if you cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot, sharp, and soothing water, and they cease to bleed, then gargle the patient with water or the rinds of lemons are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then cure them as long as they are sound; and sometimes other swellings arise in the throat than the two almonds, if you cut them in the same way as the two almonds agree.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I healed a woman from an abscess that had formed in her throat, namely a small abscess of the tonsils. It had almost completely closed off the throat, so that the woman could neither breathe nor eat or drink, and she would have been dead if she had remained like this for one day or two. The abscess was so swollen that I had to make two incisions with my needle through the two openings of the nose. Then I quickly made a stitch in one of them, then pulled out the thread, and took a large portion of gut; then refixed the other part through the other opening of the nose, and closed up her mouth and pressed down her tongue. After that, I sewed the abscess with my needle, cut off some of it, and only a little blood came out; and so was unblocked the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and ceased not to cut away from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large. Then I closed it with stitches and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stayed without growing; and I left those parts, and only knew what God did with them after me.
de l’uve	Il semble que tu aies ajouté une ligne de texte qui n'est pas liée à la traduction du texte original. "De l'uve" peut être un terme médical ancien, mais sans plus de contexte, il est difficile de savoir ce que cela signifie.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the tumour comes out to the surface and is long and thin, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is under a thick and rounded skin, it is called "uve". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and you see that the swelling of the abscess has been eased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to lance it; and that which is rounded and assembled but is not long, whether it is sanguine or of a greenish color or black. It is necessary to leave the incision alone.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take the chief a comb of hair or put ointment on it, as the men do with a spoon, and put the instrument over all the ointment on the eye; and have the patient sit beside you so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat or the wound. Then hold your hand over all the ointment and press on the eye with the quantity of a half hour until you see it turn dark brown and the medication's irritation is calmed; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the hollow of the eye up to the point that the cotton touches the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete. Then let it dry and wait four or five days.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than incision or cautery; if it is treated by smoke according to this manner: take calamus and yarrow and origanum and rue and camomile and hawthorn and similar herbs, and put all or some of them together in one pot, and I heat it up; and the pot be well glazed with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be of silver or lead, and be one of the keys stuck in the patient's mouth as long as the steam rises to the ulcer through the tube, until the ulcer is dead; then it starts again several times, until the ulcer dries up, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of hot aposteme, because many things happen; and never do this except at the decline of hot aposteme. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put inside the patient's head an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not let the steam oppress the mouth, and it is good cure together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that the sore is in the throat or the spine of a fish, or anything else; so it is necessary to treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see its movements; and if something is stuck in the throat and not apparent, it is necessary to make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of nail, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then have the patient swallow it; and when it comes up, you can see it, and then treat it accordingly. And if it doesn't come out through the means we've mentioned, take an instrument made of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and have the head raised upwards. And take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything come down upon you, nor push the bone in; and it's worth noting that the patient should insert the instrument themselves, because they will feel or see when the thing is being extracted; then they should swallow it downwards, or have it pulled out at the other end with all the force of the instrument, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous avons terminé la traduction du texte. La dernière phrase "de la sansue de la gorge" pourrait être une mention supplémentaire du problème initial dont on parle dans le texte, qui est la présence d'une odeur nauséabonde provenant de la gorge.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Il semble que nous avons recommencé à traduire le texte. Voici la traduction :
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not sweat as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asefetide, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the olive; do this many times, for it will sweat without trouble. And the manner of fumigation is such that you take one pot where there are glowing coals, and the pot is covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and inside the hole is the key to the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the tip of the cane in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up just to the nose; and the sweat will now come, and if it does not come, repeat the fumigation many times. And make the patient thirsty, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water at all; and then they must purge through this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats sweat is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved tweezers for moles to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a bird's beak, and it has an asperity of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go. li chapistres des apostemes	It seems like we have gone from a medical text to a diagram or illustration!
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many likenesses of abscesses, according to what remembrance comes after this and the other in this book, and they vary in perforation and incision; and it is in two manners, one being its own likeness, and because of moisture. And the second manner is for those that have at their body parts. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the firm parts are different from those that come into joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses which should not be pierced until the bowels are dead according to their completion; and such as require piercing when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, as an abscess near joints. For when abscesses occur near joints, and one leaves them until they are putrid around them, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, by which it is a cause of contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay the perforation so long that it becomes mortified; or it is near the fundament, if one pierces it at once when it is dead; and it should not be that you pierce an abscess which has become hard without digestion being completed, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it putrefies inwardly and becomes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary for you to know the hour of perforating the abscess which has become dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain is alleviated, and the departures of the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and redness, and the quieting down and soothing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary for you to perform the perforation in the place where it appears most dependent on the abscess, and where it opens up; and make the perforation as long as possible, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	When there is pus that flows according to the place of the member. And when an abscess is in fatty flesh, it is best to leave the perforation until it has been confirmed to have completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom will be drawn out and it will be filled with a great deal of filth; and perhaps the edges and the bottom of it will become hardened. And for certain abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, in accordance with what the member requires.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you carefully pierce it; and when the abscess is large and has drawn out a great quantity of pus, and you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus at once, but pull out a part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then take out anything from it; do this in fits and starts, as much as the pus comes out, so that the patient may live; especially if the patient is weakly or a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit men. For the stitches may sometimes tremble with the issue of the pus, lest the patient die, and you are unaware of it. Then therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if there is an opening in it, look to see if the opening in the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, then bind it up with bandages made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, it is necessary that you put a tent on each one so that they come together; and if you have covered in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have sewn it around, then fill it with old cotton or the rags of linen without moisture, and bind it until the next day; then take it out, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.
