Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to go about treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or let's talk about swellings that come on the head and are small abscesses, and they resemble boils that are in a sack, just like the swelling of a chicken's joint, and there are many similarities. There are fat ones and those that have moisture like pus; and some are hard and rocky to cut into, and one can be certain that the artery does not make it worse. And the procedure for cutting is that you prick with every instrument called an "entromissoire", from which its shape comes after, whatever thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, then you pour something over the long part. And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contained that moisture, because it will come back again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if it's present; otherwise, in water and vinegar, and plug the wound, and let it be just until the next day; and those who are left overnight will run. And then start over with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know that there is no more left overnight; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it's healed. And if the abscess remains one night fat, then cut into it according to this shape, along its length; and I will squeeze out my stitches, and scrape off from all sides, and put all your cure of drawing up the skin where it lies; and if the artery makes it worse, do what I told you after. And similarly do with an abscess that is rocky, and hard to cut into, and to cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Et maintenant parlons de l'absces qui se forme sur la tête, pierreux et à moiteur, il est plus léger car il est rempli de pus. Et s'il y a des abscesses dans le chef sans aucune humidité, comme celui que je vais te décrire, qui fut un absces sur la tête d'une femme âgée, et j'ai trouvé l'absce aussi dur qu'une pierre rugueuse et aspre, et blanc, et impossible à briser; si on en avait fait une plaie avec lui, il aurait été tout aussi malade. Et les autres abscesses qui viennent sur la tête, comme ceux qui se forment aux racines des oreilles des enfants, l'ouverture doit toujours être au maximum possible, pour que les pus puissent sortir; et on les guérit de la même manière qu'il convient.
des scrophules	swellings (likely referring to swollen lymph nodes)
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	The swelling frequently occurs in the neck and under the arms, and sometimes in other parts of the body, and they come out one after another. And each swelling is properly contained within its own spot, just like the nodes and swellings on the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these swellings are many. There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and do not want to heal.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol solution or certain powders that stop blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is alleviated, and the wound becomes soft and begins to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then inquire about your debt if there are any small scrophules left, cut them and scrape them. And if it has a large vein in the root of the scrophule, do not need to cut that scrophule at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it hang down without harm; then dress the wound with old Egyptian linen cloth, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole scrophule, it is well to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, then there will be no superfluous matter left due to the size of the scrophule. It is necessary that you understand how to cut out the root of it, and draw forth the pus, and sew it as we have said. Those scrophules which hold superfluous matter, perforate them where they are most swollen; and perforate them just like those previously mentioned, in such a way that they depend on something, then apply tents with ointment and similar things so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, dress it with ointment anointed flesh, until it be healed.

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	It seems like you've copied another passage from the text.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swallowed, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglote" be removed; and do not help by means of these things, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are hot towards those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to close the epiglote to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglote, it is necessary that we cut it under three or four circles or a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the skin incision, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those who are thus suitable for the cutting of the epiglote, it should not have flesh, and the vessels should be long enough to see.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeon is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its utmost extent, then cuts the skin as far as it will come, and stops the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the epiglote, just as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the vein from the channel which jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which we doubt the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the skin and sew all around without the cartilage; then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I advise that we do not perform this operation as far as the throat is completely closed and the patient has been judged to be dying and there is no hope for him.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglote so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and therefore the ancients commanded that the wound be left open as long as the force of the disease had passed, and it passes in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was completely healed.

et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to come and cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood was issuing from it, and I saw well that she had not cut very deeply nor far up into the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.

de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This swelling is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large tumor of a blackish color, and it occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it occurs according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or if it is a natural one, it has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one occurs in two ways: one of which is similar to fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to a swelling that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there should be fear, and it is not to be operated on with fire unless in that one which is small, and the proof and investigation is made through all the surrounding tissues.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it to be just like one fatty tumor, and it cannot be pushed in any way, then cut it out, as we would cut out an abscess, and remove the surrounding fat if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and investigate thoroughly, and heal it just as is proper, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of abscesses.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of abscesses, the likenesses of which I will describe all.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I tell you the whole difference that exists between an abscess and a fistula.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a fistula is hot and feverish, as long as the inflammation has not passed, and the purulence has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Unlike an abscess, a fistula has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains one pus-filled sac, which is its own separate sack and is of the same color as the body, and begins like a blackish spot, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either fatty or moist, and much of their color is just like I said in the division (i.e., of abscesses).
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the abscess, that you first probe and investigate it thoroughly with all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", according to what its shape may be, or a chapel that comes afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of investigating abscesses is that you take up the moistest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your probe back and forth, so that you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then you proceed according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then pull out the probe, and pay attention to what comes out with it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moist core comes out, whatever its color may be, then cut it out, as I said about other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the probe there comes out a moist core, know that it is fatty, then cut it out in a cross shape, and take hold of it with pincers, and scrape off its outer layer lightly from each part, and then bind it up in a cloth where you will draw it out well and heal it with the abscess.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then take it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will come back as an abscess many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a small piece remains and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some sharp caustic powders, and bind the wound tight, and apply warm soothing things to the abscess, and heal it with other treatments until it is completely healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the abscess is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with those things that corrode flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is bleeding too much or otherwise contrary to your treatment, then apply the vitriol paste and let it stay for two or three days, until the wound purifies, and the inflammation of the blood subsides; then come back to cut out what remains of the abscess.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Look at the shapes of the entromissoire instruments, and they are in three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three square ones that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three kinds of them: large, medium, and small, to investigate the abscesses of fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one cuts out sorceles, and they are made of yellow tin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more suitable for piercing black boils to investigate the carbuncles of fistulas.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the diameter of the fistula's opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the probes are of many likenesses, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are also probes with two curved parts, in three manners alike.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are probes with three curved parts, and they also come in three manners; and there are also probes with two curved parts, and probes with a single curved part, and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these probes are cutting, and there are some that do not cut at all, except from one side, which is used to scrape out the abscess, because they do not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and among these probes are the handles wrapped in cloth, so that the patient does not feel them when they open up the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see here.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they are not used at all except for in the fleshier parts, such as legs, arms, and shoulders, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a file for cutting iron, in this shape, to staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place where veins and arteries are cut open, and it is also made in this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of certain men become inflamed when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like female breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, should do so according to the shape of this line b, up to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with flesh-corrosive medication, then sew together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and cure it until it is completely healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops downward and is swollen due to its size like in women, then it should be sewn up in two seams above, through two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this shape, from line b up to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and everything necessary for the treatment, until it is completely healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not completely closed because the patient does not want to rest or because of the discharge of pus, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be so that the remaining and the fat are melted, then cure it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The abscesses of the buttocks.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are a type of hard scrofula with edges, and there are some that contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain pus should be cut out according to this shape, from line b up to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire boil that is in the abscess has been drained, you should fill the wound with old cloth and let it stay until the next day, then remove all the cloth and treat it with ointment suitable for this treatment until it is completely healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, then treat it in the same way as we have said for scrofulas with incisions, and if the wound becomes infected again, apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The rupture of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn up, then abscesses come again many times, and it also happens that the vein becomes swollen and forms an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows to recognize this when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, you feel a hardening; and when it is due to the vein, it appears swollen on the surface.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolishness to cut out this abscess, and similarly when it is under the buttocks, armpits, and neck, and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	So then it is necessary to delay the treatment with iron, and also the one who is in charge should delay as well, and for those with swelling of an artery, make an incision above the skin from where it is long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the size with probes, and carefully separate the artery from its covering, until it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle under it and pierce it up to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place between the two threads with a probe until the blood comes out that was there, and let the abscess be loosened.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that causes pus to come out, until the swelling subsides.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with suitable ointment, until it is completely healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the cutting of a vein, then it is necessary that you mark with your hand the entire skin where you can draw out pus from the abscess.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the place that you have marked on your hand, and pierce it through, and there will be a double thread, so that you can pull it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie off the abscess, just like I told you, or tie one end of the two threads to each of the eyes of the needle.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you are unsure that the thread will come out, then insert another needle through all of the thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut out the abscess until the excess tissue comes out, and then cut out the excess skin and leave what is left tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a moist linen bandage soaked in wine and oil, and then apply treatments of tents and ointments until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des ners	The abscesses of the neck.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to abscesses that come in the artery and vein, there are abscesses that occur in the neck when it is cut or due to excessive work or similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the armpits and hands and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of flesh, and it is in various conditions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but rather under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it can move well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor above or below, and the one that is in joints should not be cut by iron: perhaps there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one that is on the head or forehead, make an incision in the skin to allow it to breathe.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, tie it with forceps and cut out its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a probe and scrape out the pus, then remove it and sew together the wound at the seam, and treat it until it is completely healed.
des grosses boces pendans	The large hanging hives.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it appears in bellies and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "fungus" by the resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is subtle and its head is large; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen one man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had a small root, were cut off, and were dripping with pus.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found one to weigh 28 ounces, and the other 5 pounds, and the work in the incision is such that you look at it and see that the patient's body is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	so I cut them out at the navel's width, and were in your presence the cautery over the fire. Because when you cut it there come often too great discharges of blood, and if the bleeding does not stop, then you hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient showing signs of anxiety and fear of the incision with iron, then take a well-made cord of linen and tie the tumor as we have said, and let it stay for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then pull it tight, and do not stop pulling the linen cord until the tumor is cut out, and use it as an aid in the surgery; and if the roots are large, be careful to cut them out entirely from the belly, but you can safely cut off half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	and then cauterize it so that it does not recur; then treat the wound and be careful that you do not cut out the tumor which is of a bad color, poor sensation, and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of a chancre later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil has burst.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a boil comes from cauterization of a wound or an incision made by a syphilis sore, and is on the belly and in some of the boils, as it happens with other eruptions, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is due to the ulceration of the syphilis and from the emergence of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and has various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the emergence of the intestine, then it is even more varied. When you press it with your hands it swells up and then returns to its normal shape, and perhaps it becomes swollen, and grows very large at the entrance of the boil and due to hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to pus, then it is a light thing and bursts well when you press it with your hand, without being forced. And if it is due to blood, it bursts with these signs of a large and hard abscess, and is filled according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, then it feels soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look and see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You should leave the treatment alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the swelling is due to the intestine or bowel, then you should command the patient to evacuate his intestines and stretch it straight out, then bind it all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to lie on his back with it supported by your hands.
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have bound all along the body.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch the top half of the abscess to the great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread or a tight cord of strong silk firmly, and let the two ends be tied together.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the top half of the abscess that is stretched over the ligament, and insert your index finger, and close the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the ligament, then untie it, and push the intestine through to the outside of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, then take hold of it with the forceps, and cut out the redundancy;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or the vein is contrary, go carefully around them, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two fine threads into them, and put the two needles through what you have done in a cross shape where you made the piercing;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then draw the abscess into four parts above the needles, and if it seems to you, remove the needles, and let the place be as long as it will drain, and cut out the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can cut it when it is softened and drained, then clean up the remaining parts as needed, and close the abscess just like we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture you find, then treat the place as it becomes necessary, and bind the place.
dou chancre	a boil
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the signs of boils and how to work with medicines and how to avoid treating with iron; and we say that boils start in the groin area and great care is needed in their cure, and the ancient ones said that when a boil is in an area where it can be cut out like those on the breasts and thighs and similar areas, and you must remove all of them when they are at the beginning; and when they are old and large, then you should not approach them, for I have never seen anyone healed from them; nor has anyone ever been cured in front of me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in an area where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make them clean if they have manifest repletion; then prepare the patient to be made well, i.e. a good place for doing the operation; then cut out or remove the boil, and scrape off all its scabs, and take it out from all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood dry completely, and squeeze the area with your hand or something else, and if there are discolorations of blood that make you contrary to the incision of an artery or a vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until they are healed.
de ydropisie	It seems like we've switched topics!
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: there remains only one; and you should not touch with iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly thing; then when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as colic and solution of the belly and similar things; do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and when you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is not too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient up straight in front of you, and have the servants push the belly down, forcing out the water to the lowest part of the abdomen. Then take the spathum ileus (a type of surgical instrument) according to this shape: it should be cut off at two points, with a point; and in any case, it should not be so sharp that it can reach as far as the intestine when you insert it, and it should not cause bleeding.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the dropsy is running towards the intestines: if so, you will need to cut up the belly 3 fingers' breadth above the navel; and if it's due to disease of the liver, the incision should be on the left side of the belly, 3 fingers' breadth above the navel. If it's due to a tumor, the incision should be on the right side, and it must not be such that the patient lies on top of the incision so that the superfluous fluids can flow into that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin with the instrument and push it in, and lift your hand to take out all of the spathum ileus between the skin and the fascia, just as when you are scraping away to the size of a fingernail or slightly more. Then pierce the fascia so that the spathum ileus comes out at the lower part, which is the place where the water is; then remove the instrument and put this one in its place, which has the shape: it looks like a thin silver cord, and is made of lead or of archaunt (an alloy) that is light, and on one side there is 1 small perforation, and on the other side there are 3 perforations. And on the third side there are 2 perforations, and 1 on the other; and the key is cut so as to be like a feather, and it's the shape of the incision that the scribes draw with their quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alemele (a type of drainage valve), so that when the instrument comes to the water, they now lift it up on top of the instrument. Empty then one third or half, for if you empty more than it's necessary at this hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit out of the body, or they'll faint, or come close to death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But in voidance according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the indications of the patient's virtue signify, and his hairs; then take the instrument and hold the blade, and it is held now for the cure which stops the hole that is on the scrotum, of which I spoke, so that you pierce in this manner; then reattach the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. And when he wants to urinate, have it taken out, let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it will not be necessary, because the urine that comes out is not left closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small can be cured with medicines made from cloth, as we have said, and it will expand. Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez. de la circoncision	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La circoncision est un procédé médical qui consiste à retirer le prépuce, une partie du pénis chez l'homme, généralement pour des raisons religieuses ou hygiéniques.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not separation of continuation like other wounds; however when we do this work of our own will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not instruct their children to be circumcised, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.

For I have seen the majority of masters and sages who performed circumcision around an infant's genitals, with forceps and all sorts of novelties; it was a chase because there are two foreskins, and perhaps if one is cut off above, the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut. dou retenement de l’urine	Il semble que vous souhaitez discuter d'un sujet médical spécifique. Si vous voulez, nous pouvons parler d'un autre sujet.

des maladies de la vessie	of bladder disorders

de la piere	It seems like we've reached the end of this text! "De la pierre" is likely a phrase indicating that the instructions are being concluded.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément. et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, sprinkle the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place above it one cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then let the patient rise on their neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, wash the wound thoroughly with oil and water; then treat it with refined ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses come to the wound and corrosion, and congealed blood in the bladder, and it is retained the urine, which comes out in that manner without passing with the urine: then heat your dough in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, they will corrode the bladder, and the patient will perish.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then raise the wound with water and egg white and silk, and help him in all ways that you see, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you cure him, that you tie together the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the conduit of the penis, and fixed inside, and urine cannot come out; then I advise you to treat him with what I said before, that you cut into it many times, for a good excuse for cutting is this cure. I have already tried it this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this shape and it must have three spiked ends attached to one end of the shaft.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a string and tie it around the handle of the iron rod near the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the rod into the handle slightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod back to your hand with the stone facing you, poking in and out slowly, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what is left of the stone inside the handle. If it breaks apart immediately, it will shoot forth with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because something is hindering it, then tie one string under the stone and another above it, then place the handle in front of the stone between the two strings, then pull it out, and loosen the string, and clean the frozen blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	What happens when the stone is stuck in women, and if it ever does happen, it's a serious cure, and it's prevented for three reasons: one is that maybe the woman is still a virgin; and the second is that you can't find a well-educated woman who will show herself to the mirrors, especially during her menstrual period.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third reason is that maybe you can't find a well-educated woman who knows this art by hand; and the fourth reason is that the woman's stone is often deeper inside than the man's stone, so it needs to be cut more deeply, and there is great fear in doing so.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need to, summon a midwife who is well-versed in this matter, and at times it can be found among them, and if you cannot find one, then choose an experienced and skilled woman, such as a female surgeon or someone who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order regarding the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And examine her well to see if the woman is still a virgin: then you need to press your thumb or handle against the foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her thumb, and advise her to push her thumb or handle into the wound, and guide and press her left hand on top of the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then you need to guide her in moving the stone gradually from the entrance of the bladder up to its base, all the way until it reaches the root of the thigh. Then press upwards on the stone at the root of the thigh, against the midpoint of the intestine, where the appearance is most noticeable, and feel for the stone in that area. And do not move your thumb above or below the stone, but keep it at a slight angle.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then place your right thumb in the incision, if you feel the stone so close to the wound that it can come out freely, and know that there are many types of stones: that is to say, small and large ones, rough and smooth ones, long and round ones, and those with ridges. If you know their characteristics, you will be able to recognize them and predict the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the vein is swollen, put vitriol powder on it and hold it in place for an hour until the swelling is reduced; then return to your work, until the stone is heated, and have instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you with your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the swelling is due to an artery that has been cut, put powder on the place and use tents and bandages to stop it from bleeding again, and leave the stone alone and do not touch it at all, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is cooled down and the swelling has subsided, then return to your work, until the stone is heated.
de hernie carnouse	of a flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Tubal waters are nothing other than an accumulation of mucus or white fluid, which is located below the shell of the ovary that contains the egg; and it is called "tubal fluid", and sometimes it is properly contained in the membrane of the ovary, so one thinks it to be another egg; and this is the skin of the ovary between the white tubal fluid that we have mentioned; and these things do not belong.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the origin of this tubal water is a weakness that comes to the ovaries, and it spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the ovaries, and this mucus has many colors: or it's colored with yellowish tints, or without red, or black, or pale blue, and so on.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this accumulation: because if it is white tubal fluid that we have mentioned, then it is a reclusive growth, i.e. a long pouch like the shape of an egg, and it does not open the ovary, because it has mucus all around it.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has mucus in the proper membrane, then it is a reclusive growth with a part of the egg, and for that reason one thinks it to be another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the mucus is between the skin of the ovary and the white tubal fluid, then it smells very bad; therefore, when you want to know the color of the mucus, stir up all the surrounding tissues to see what shape it has taken on before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, then, what happens after the mucus has been stirred up, judge from that what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cut it with iron, it should be cured according to its illness and the filling of its body; then have a servant stand on its back, on something somewhat high, and place underneath him a lot of linen.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on its left side, and command the servant to sit on the right, and extend the rod (or sword) towards one of the two edges of the skin of the ovaries.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the scalpel (spatumile) left-handed, and cut the skin of the ovary between the long part and close to the handle, so that the incision is straight and divides the skin of the ovary up to the white tubal fluid, and then peel it away carefully as possible.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the tubal fluid with a needle to one large puncture, and extract all the fluid, and then put in some hot oil (oncines), and spread the tubal fluid upwards; and do not touch the skin of the ovary, but only the tubal fluid itself. Cut out any pieces of it carefully, even the surrounding tissue on both sides, so that if you don't cut it well, the fluid will come back.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg drops out of its place in your hands, remove it from its location when you have completed the work on the tubal fluid; then sew together the two flaps of the skin of the ovary with a suture, and then treat it as one would any other wound, so that it is cured.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the uterus corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended in doubt of bleeding; then scrape the cervix to the entire suspension, and extract the uterus, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the eye is assembled into two parts together, know that they are two nerves; if you scrape the other part as you have done with the first equally, then spew out the blood, and put in the wound a wet linen cloth in rosed oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another wet linen cloth in wine and oil on top of it, and put the two cervixes on top, and put double cloths above, and tie it up above with all the thread that is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with tow according to this likeness and have them sewn together by seam in the crotch of the breeches, and let one of the ends reach up to the fundament just to the back, and the other to the part of the groin; and the other end on top of the two corners, and be entirely assembled the restriction within the loop of the breech.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and at any time medicine this nerve with a cauter in place of the iron stylus, and it is that you take one cauter slender, and scrape the skin of the cervix, and be heated as we have said, so that the white filigree that contains the eye is uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cauter according to this form, and pierce that filigree once, and scrape it with that slender cauter hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cautery in all ways that you can, until you exhaust everything; and be sure that fire does not touch the uterus; and know that this work is more safe; and also beware of hemorrhage of blood, and beware of the works of cutting.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing contrary is done, or an abscess forms or hemorrhage of blood or other thing, then treat what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then make a perforation, as I told you, and know that once you are well certain by the signs which we have said that ramica aquosa is lost,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then make the patient sit on the high seat; then pierce the abscess at the lower part up to the whole spatium in width, and put the perforation from long of the body; and let the hole be wide so that all the water may flow out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let it flow out the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not let the water come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must put a pin or the instrument with which one treats the water from dropsies, whose shape is as before; and enlarge this small pouch of the wound, and know that the water will return and be assembled after 6 months or thereabouts, and when it is assembled like before, then the patient will pass their days.
