de la routure dou syfac	of the twisting of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The consequences of this stricture are through the incision that comes out of the spleen, or the stretching above the stomach in the part of the groin, because the intestines descend from that twisting to one of the scrotums;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this stricture is either of the spleen or from its stretching, and come these two manners of different causes: or from a blow, or from a jump, or from a hard burden, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the stretching of the spleen, are that there have been pains and aches, over a long time, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscess is equal from top to bottom, because the spleen presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the incision of the spleen, that a sudden pain comes at the beginning, and the abscess appears in different forms under the skin nearby, because of the issue of the intestine and the body from the far part of the spleen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at all times they [the intestines] descend with the spleen and are retained in that way, and cause great pain to suffer the sick person, especially when it is compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And with these treatments of iron powder to pour on [the wound], why does he take the risk to recover?
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the operation is that you command the sick person to reach in with his hand and retrieve the intestine from the wound, if he can get it inside.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let him be sewn on top of his neck between your hands, and lift up the scrotum.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then take a knife above [the intestines] and cut all the skin of the thighs from long [down to the scrotum].
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the flaps of the abdomen needles according to what you need to open the wound, and have them sewn in such a way that the entrails can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape off the spleen that is under the skin of the thighs, until the white and hard part of the spleen is exposed on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then put your thumb and index finger in the area between the skin and the white spleen that is under the membrane of the ovary, and between the second spleen.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and tear what is behind the ovary, and between the second spleen; and then move with your right hand inside the skin of the thighs, and pull out the white spleen upwards to your left hand, and lift up the ovary along with all its spleen towards the abdomen.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the assistant to stretch out the ovary upwards, and untie what is tied behind it.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your fingers if there is any part of the intestine that has slipped into the white spleen or hardened part, and if you find anything, put it inside the abdomen.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle where it has a big thread made of 6 threads, and put it in the back part of the spleen, which is after the skin of the thighs, then through the abdomen, and then cut off the ends of the threads so that there are 4 threads remaining.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then gather them up one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the spleen that we mentioned which is under the skin of the thighs with a strong knot of 2 parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then surround the shoulders of boys with linen wraps, and tie them tightly in two parts, so that none of their servants who feed them can enter into them, lest an abscess forms there.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place a linen cloth over the first band, two fingers in length from it, and after these two bands let down the scrotum that is under the skin of the testicles to the size of one finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that the rest to the roundness that the testicles bear; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles, so as to make it smooth and rounded, as we said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moistened wool in oil, put on the wounds, and then apply the band that we have spoken of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white skin that we have said to cauterize after the incision, due to fear of blood discharging.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this has happened many times, and leave the band on until it heals itself; and if it takes time to heal, then cauterize with hot water, and apply what we have said above, until it heals.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	It looks like we've moved on to a new topic.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	I am never seen a person who dared to make the treatment by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancient ones said that it is done in such a way as the ramie plant which is tied to the eye, in such a manner that you tie the wasps, afterwards hanging from above lightly under.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cover it with me, and treat the abscess of him who works, as long as the wasps are bleeding; and cure it in such a way as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Whenever the intestine comes out of the anus, as we have said, and opens up the place; and let no intestine come out into the scrotum, and if it does come out, that is a sign, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and in any case, if it stays too long in this place, the wound or hernia becomes inflamed, until the intestine comes out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and those things happen by the extension of the hernia which is at the anus, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and inflamed the place and opens up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before; and in any case it is cured by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and that the patient lies on his back with you in your hands, then cut the place of the hernia inflamed by a width according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the hernia which is under the skin that follows, and take the iron and put it on the place of the visible hernia.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press hard into the belly, then sew the two visible places of the hernia on top of the iron rod, and sew one and the other together.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	and then pull out the iron rod, and do not sew the hernia or stretch the bowels or anything else, as I have shown you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and then heal it by the cure for wounds. And when you sew the threads, if they do not come out and the wound is healed, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syrup is thickened, and has no appearance in the texture, and the cautery is most beneficial in this place, and more close to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from softening of the skin of the groin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the groin is often softened in certain men, because the veins inside them are made soft, and it can be seen; and when you want to treat it, you make the patient lie on their back, and cut out the softened skin from over the natural skin; then sew together the two lips with a suture, and if you see fit, sew first the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches tightly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the flagellation (or whipping)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	It is known that flagellation is prescribed in our law, and because of this I would like it to be mentioned in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one of which is that physicians are instructed to respond when asked, and how to treat the wounds; and the other, because we often need to flagellate certain beasts to help us, such as goats, sheep, and horses, and other beasts. I say therefore that flagellation is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by tearing apart. In the case of doing it by attraction, you make the beast sit in hot water until the groin are softened and during; then take them at hand, until they return to normal and you feel them no more. Regarding flagellation by tearing: it is necessary that you tie the beast, press the skin of the groin with your left hand, then tie the suspenders, and cut above each opening in one blow, when you have well cleansed them; and I leave some pus from the syrup and the subtle syrup that is on the vessels; and this manner of flagellation is more beneficial than the one done by attraction, because in the attraction perhaps something remains from the groin, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	La matière de ces hermophrodites est tres obscure et tres difficile a traiter, car il ne sont pas des hommes, ny des femmes, mais les parties de l'un et l'autre se trouvent en eux.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodity is according to two manners as men: one is that between the two testicles it opens just like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes pours out urine. And the other manner is in women, and he has on the tip just like a penis and two testicles. And the cure for man and woman is that you bind up the joined parts all together, and cure them just like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	The tenthigenie (a reference to Theophrastus' Characters or possibly an error)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a joined part on the natural place, as long as it's too ugly to see; and some women have just as big one as a hand, and that's what needs to be cured. You need to dye off the excess of the tentigene to your hand or fingers, and bind it lightly; and don't go too deep in, lest bleeding occurs from there, then cure it with another treatment until it heals; and there is another wound that appears at the mouth of the womb, and you apply a poultice, and by chance it bursts forth, and resembles the appearance of an cow, and for this reason they called it in old times "cow disease". It's necessary to bind it, just as we said about the tentigene, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	La description semble être un texte médical ancien, possible du Moyen Âge ou de la Renaissance.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Here is the translation of the text:
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not have a cutaneous opening; and when hemorrhoids become old they become thrombosed. We have already spoken in the division about their likenesses and signs, and I will speak now about those which receive cure. I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosis, when they are quite formed in the rectum and do not appear to the sense, cannot be cured by cutting. Those which are at the entrance of the rectum, which can be felt, are those which can be cured. You must then put the woman into a cold house, afterwards anoint the thrombosis with torches, and the root with medicine-restraining blood, such as myrrh and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the outside of it for an hour, then place her in cold water. If there is bleeding which comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and gall, and make a poultice on her back. And if she stops [bleeding], it is good. If not, make the ventouses adhere to the back and the shoulders so that they hurt; then take linen and moisten it in plantain juice or in violets' juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. And when the swelling subsides, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and "albathir" which means red, is similar to a harsh head, so cover it as I said for thrombosis, and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Les apostèmes de la marris (rectum) ! C'est un sujet sensible, mais je vais essayer de fournir une traduction et des informations utiles.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come to the groin, such as chancre and hot abscess and herpes and boilstones and fistules and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. It is necessary for me to say in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes to the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that cools down; and if you want to know how to do it with fire, look if the abscess is swollen at its beginning when it arrives, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it. Then do not hasten to puncture, but let it subside as long as the pain is calmed; and then have the patient sit on a stool with two small stools under which he reclines, and support him back and put his legs out to the sides of the knee; and his thighs are spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then make the instrument approach from the right side, and it will bring forth the form; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you stick the first needle into it to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloth, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary to put the nozzle of the instrument above, and to tie the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and they do it with a soft hand, then you must close it at the head, at the left side of the spatulum; and when the bowel is empty, then it is necessary for you to put dampened linen cloths in rose oil or greenish oil into the wound; and put the cloth deep inside the groin, and put a clean, moistened linen bandage on top of the groin and the handle, then cure after two days of suitable ointment until they are healed; and sometimes lift the groin and the wound with a poultice of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristologe long enough cooked, then return to the ointment. And if the wound is re-opened in the groin, it is necessary that you beware of cooking with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Je vous ai mal compris ! Vous voulez que je traduise le texte médical en anglais moderne, n'est-ce pas ? Désolé pour la confusion !
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs: when you see the woman hastening to go down below and desires to smell the air; then the child rushes out; so you know that this child is according to the natural figure, and it comes out through its head and second toe together. And when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child may come out quickly; for when it goes up through its head, the second toe comes with it, and there is good purging of the mother's superfluities by good purification.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out through its head by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtues of the child are weak, make her sit on a stool, or have the women hold her; and prepare an oil or fenugreek paste that has been cooked, and then have the midwife give it to her between her teeth as a small spatula.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment. de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins

de l’enfant mort	of a dead child

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (meaning: to insert something into the anus)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle scab.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Thus it is necessary for the woman to have him pierce that scab with her finger, and not to pierce him with a sharp spatula, and to grasp the ligament so that she doesn't touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on linen soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it won't close again, then put or insert a plug of linen, and let it stay for a while, and be removed when the baby wants to go into the chambers (meaning: when the baby is born).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And any time this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary to close that sudden opening: if it is cured, as we have said of the linen plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	about the fistula in the fundament (meaning: anal fistula)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Abscesses that come from underneath the fundament are swelling, and those that come from above the fundament or between the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or more than one; and when that swelling is old, it works, and in the meantime, moist heat softens or subtly whitens.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and at times these fistulas persist; and they are known by those who are or are expelled from them or by flatulence when the patient makes an effort to pass gas, and possibly in the sound of vomiting.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the join of the thigh, and just to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows a persistent fistula at the fundament, and not persisting:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you probe your toe or fundament, and probe a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then I probe a thin thread of linen or a horse's hair, so that you feel the thread or the hair at your toe;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there does not come through a passage of gas or wind or vomit, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not penetrate; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent right up to the bladder or to the channel of urine, if it causes the urine to flow out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	Since it is pierced right up to the join of the thigh, then the thread comes out at the knee.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	since there is no twisting and the cause of the pain is nearby, it means that it has pierced deep into the bowel, and does not help medicine or suturing by anointing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no strong cure except for surgery, and the vanity of foolish surgeons who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are not persistent and not old, there is hope for recovery by iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and is that the patient lies between your hands on their back, and lifts their legs up to their thighs, and has their thighs bent towards their stomach.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then probe a thread of silver or linen if there is twisting, so that you know when the thread comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around their fundament, then it seems best to probe with your index finger,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if then you feel that the thread has pierced; and if you discover with your finger between your toe the sinew or flesh, at that moment know that it is persistent.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	and there's no point trying to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We say that some can be healed well, but that is rare.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the treatment we give is to cauterize the area subtly according to the size of the fistula, as it was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and make it hot in the fistula, until it comes out near the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that the charred tissues are burned, which are resembling a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then heal it with damp threads in butter, as long as the burned tissues come out further; and then heal it with an ointment that draws out scab and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus cleansed, it is well. If not, otherwise cannot be cleansed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the fistula comes out and does not pierce all the way to the root which is at the foundation, and between your navel and the fistula is a cover made of fat or of silk, and you see the fistula come out through this cover.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you take a cloth from the beginning of the fistula and stop it there immediately before the tent, and burn the cauter after, as long as it comes to the top of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the fistula will be delivered and dry up; then cut off those dead fats that seem like a bird's feather, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the abscess swells and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or a strong medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For cauterizations of fire bring together two good things: that is to say, the burning of these gathered fats and the drying of blood and moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the wound of moist tents in butter or in cheese broth, as long as the pus drips out and issues the burned fats into the bowel.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then heal the wound with ointments of solid unguents that dry hard fat, and are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For once it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the foundation and is far from the body, then plug it with your navel or foundation, and seek it out.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and there are two threads, whether it is linen or silk or fat, or if it is near to piercing, then there should not be fire that you see of faith and hope, through the administration of one of three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	when you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it straight to the bottom, or if you can see any putrid parts and cure them as first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and don't go too deep, lest you cut the tendons that hold the foundation, and come to the evacuations by an involuntary sense.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be cured, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut near the foundation, either by probing or with another instrument designed for this purpose.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse the foul carrion that is in the wound as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then try to restore the wound and to close the fistula in the part outside the foundation; if this is an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And whenever her fistulas are according to this manner: and is when you insert the probe in the fistula, and it is on either side of the foundation near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a sharp-tipped probe at its head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I insert one thread in two, and insert the probe into all the thread in the fistula as far as its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced on the edge of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that perforated one, in the same way as you insert your probe into the other side of the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull out the head of the thread, and gather together the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and leave it for one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it every time, until the threads have cut through those char things that are between them, and they bleed.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound as long as it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then have it pierced in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not seem fitting to cover the wound if it is that deep inside, and then have it healed, as we said, until it is completely sound.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinal vertebra from which they make the fistula is very much curved in one part and sharp-edged.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other part it is not, therefore we do not cover what should not be covered, as you see here:
des emorroydes	bleedings
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Bleedings are in two ways: or they are inside the fundament, as small and large grains of resin, and on the surface they dry quickly.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have a lot of moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and on the surface they have a little bit of clear water or a little bit of blood, and have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the fundament is that you command the sick person to strain themselves in a chamber, so that the fundament comes out and appears as a son.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if it's urgent, and you can grasp it with tweezers, or hold it at your fingernail, then cover its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the bleeding won't stop due to its moisture, then take it in one cloth, or cotton, or a piece of linen.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your hands, then cover them, and powder them on some hot powders that are in place of cauterizing.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then cure them with other remedies until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot come out, then purge the sick person with a bitter and sharp cathartic to wash what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the sick person feels themselves, and when the filament is outside of the fundament, then the remedy is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cover them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the cut by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you make a suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put the end of the needle into it, and then pull the thread up and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread against the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too long; and bind the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to cover up any excess bleeding;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the base a dampened cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the base, and command the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until he is urinating, and when they are done, have them treated with ointment and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the scabbing of the flesh or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is scabbing of the flesh in the intestine, and due to constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you scrape to the tip of an abscess or to the top of your fingernail with the scab on it, so that it doesn't remain moist;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it as long as is necessary until it is sound again.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then scrape more strongly than before, as long as it remains moist, and until the scab is formed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of or about a boil (or abscess)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A carbuncle is a small, false appearance on the body, and goes deep within.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and at times it finds its way to the bone, and the sensation is the same as for a boil, and comes out all over the body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread from a goose quill or a strong bird's feather, and put that thread on the boil, until the red circles go all around the boil.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to wrap up all of the thread until you go around the whole boil, and put it deep inside, and squeeze out the boil from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make a thread of copper or iron in this shape, and be subtle underneath and twisted on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that the heat may hold to the inside, and squeeze it And if you wish, scorch or cauterize the boil with a hot iron, as it is done in front of a cauterizer's shop.
de la forme dou clistere	in the shape of a catheter (or syringe)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times one makes a catheter of silver or gold, or melted copper or maillet (a type of metal), and at times one makes these instruments small and large, according to the use for which they are made.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small and large catheter is as above, with a wide head or mouth, or the belly (or bulb) is joined in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening or the belly is joined in this manner, as you see, and the nozzle (or channel) is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly is where the medicine is put from a animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each hole there is a space of one finger's breadth, then put in those holes one strong thread of twisted linen thread around ten or eleven times, and gather the belly together as a she-goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then catheterize; and that's the shape of a ring.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the catheter with oil or egg yolk, or a similar thing, then put it in gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the attendants should press the catheter with their two hands together until it is fully inflated, then extract the catheter, and lift up the sick person's legs to the bed.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine needs to come out, then tie it as tight as it can be; and if he sleeps a whole night like that, it is even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize in the disease of obstipation or constipation of the belly, and the medicine comes out quickly, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are or were a tumor, or an abscess, then the catheter should be as subtle and small as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that's the shape of a fine catheter on which the skin is tightly stretched.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatment of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and with what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things with which wounds are made are by means of stone casting, and cutting with sword or knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or are made according to the parts of the body, such as wounds that fall on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will start with head wounds that are simple, because the memory of it will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it was caused by a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt a little of an abscess forming because if the wound starts to heal quickly, with a pus coming out from the wound, and it heals on the contrary side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and feed the sick person with wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, then thin his food, and do not let him drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply a poultice on the wound, if an abscess comes to form, with a moist cotton cloth soaked in rose oil or vinegar.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess coming to form, then apply on the wound, if it is fresh and still has all its blood, and it has not been touched by air, powder, which I will speak of later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the scab has formed, then apply some ointments on it until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar thing, and the edges cannot be closed by stitches, then close them with sutures, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	And if the wound is exposed to the bone and it bleeds, and it only holds by a thread, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the sick person to eat thick meats, such as roasted capons and wheat bread, also chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a putrid skin that has not reached the bone, then scrape out all the putrid flesh and clean it well, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by means of a compress and it does not stop bleeding with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it severed, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it's that you put on this powder which soothes as soon as the scab has formed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making this powder is: take incense one part; blood of dragon two parts; and live chalk three parts, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and let it form a scab, until it is well-formed and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then tie it well, and let it be without being untied, if it swells, because the medicine is not removed until it has healed completely.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with just chalk alone, when there is not incense nor blood of dragon, but only after the scab has formed on the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the scab has formed well in its place, then do not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested ointments, or poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it is well-gone.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy than to let it alone and not put anything that is restraining on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the wound be treated with soothing medicine, such as chalk that has been washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber that has also been washed in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other powders made by mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up with stitches and tie it with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have become infected and are full of pus, then lance them or open them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes from it, then uncover it, loosen it, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spinal cord of the neck is cut or the nerves are damaged, and the conduit that carries the flesh is kept, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew up the nerve above the vertebra of the neck, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural position.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then tie it up gently and leave it for some days, then treat him with unguents of dissolving herbs until he is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then take them all out if you can, and that which you cannot get out, leave it until the wound putsrefies.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be severed and stitched up the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, look to see if there is windiness in the wound towards the inside of the sick person, then you will know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it in the first hour nor tie it for the blood that may ooze out from within.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and revive to the heart, and kill the sick person. (Note: This sentence is a bit dark and could be interpreted in different ways. In medical terms, it might mean that if the blood flow is restored, the patient may recover, but I want to clarify that the original text was written in a style more typical of medieval medical texts and may not reflect modern medical ethics.)
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but then apply an attracting ointment, and tie it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out more moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the sick person sleep on top of the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor drawing of the intestines.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure him with stitches and other treatments until he is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and suppurate, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife and it is superficial, or deeper on the front or back, then treat it as one would treat any other wound in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, sew it up with stitches; if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it has made an impression in the bone and has cut into pieces, scrape out the wound and take out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not detached, then let the wound putrefy and it will loosen the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, follow the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great, moderate and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound that sometimes lets out the intestines or the nerves of the intestines, through which their introduction comes.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worth less than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this, one puts the intestines back in more by pins, if they are not put back in warm to warm.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell at once when they feel the cold, and therefore go back into place more by pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this, a moderate wound is worth more, because one stitches the intestine back to its place twice, like other wounds.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other special stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and in any case they are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will say each one and declare them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I will translate the given Old French text into English.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and there is something to put back, this is by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are inflamed by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one soft cloth in hot water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in water with squinnt and cypress and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and wrap the intestine so that the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at once bind up the wound, and it will be quiet only to swell again.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, then wrap the intestine in hot water or broth and let the galls be cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this is alleviated the wound to a good degree;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which we use to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is better than the knife,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	for we should not cut it without great necessity if we can avoid it.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument for cutting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	cut down into the curve and back not, and behold here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is widened and the intestine bursts out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its place according to its natural shape.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able to, for this is the best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is advisable that you have him lie on his back over a bolster,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put his head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the bruise of the belly is in one of the two sides,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then position yourself so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is advisable to remember what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, apply what appears to you.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take the sore in your hands, i.e., have it ministered with poultice that clings to all the flesh on its hand.
et assemble les levres;	and sew up the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common way of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the beginning of the wound, i.e., two inches' space, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the leather with the two heads of the scabbard.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is underneath the leather inside, until you make it pierce through from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and sew up the two heads of the scabbard, and put together four;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then wrap with a doubled thread around the needle by two parts.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and sew up the two heads of the wound together.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one inch's space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just as you tied the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing it in this way with the needles, as long as you need them.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is tied together;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and then are the needles worn out, between fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the very fine needles pierce all the flesh, and the ones too thick cannot penetrate well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is fitting that they be worn out.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not suit to push the needles too far into the flesh and the leather,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they will pierce and open the wound in front of the stitch.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to prevent them from rusting.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is sown.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it only needs one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you sew together the two heads of the leather and the two heads of the scabbard, together with one needle which has a very strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these heads together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then you turn the needle at the part where you started, in the way that people sew clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave space between each stitch the thickness of a small finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	This stitch is known to men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that was in the belly of a horse.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a hand's width long.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were hanging out, two hands' widths long.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly itself.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestines, and it had been that way for twenty-four hours or more.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was stitched up in just fifteen days, and he healed, and was completely cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and they didn't heal him with ointment, because I was in one place where there wasn't any to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put old cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was completely healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the skin straight through, then leave the head of the scabbard or leather where you pushed in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inner part to the outer part;
