et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as a furrier makes pelts.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you leave it once with the scabbard on one side and take it up again from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of stitching, which Galen calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is that in which people assemble the two parts together naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one end of the scabbard to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle into the end of the leather close by, and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two heads of the scabbard.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with both heads of the scabbard;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, in two other holes of the leather which are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galeno said these words, and many others confirm them,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must put one needle from this side and the other from that side, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when a tear is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitch more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, and the scar has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	it is put together again the intestine and the cut; then put on the powder of aromatic charcoal.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the scar has changed, it is applied some ointment that is present, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and remove the thread, and sew up the scabbard and the leather.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as the others, until it is completely healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, put on old cotton, as soon as it starts to close up.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is completely healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine, except in cases where the wounds are complex;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will make a commotion among the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	you must consider that you moisten linen lightly with warm temperate oil, or rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the joints and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or burning in the bowels, and it happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then give them enemas with black wine vinegar, and especially if the burning comes up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestines called "jun" cannot heal if they are hurt,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the fragility of the veins that they are in, and the subtlety of all the body, and the closeness to its nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out of the wound, then put it back in as with the intestines, while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, then consider that you tie the place that is black, so that no bleeding comes from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the stitches.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from the part under the wound to the outside in order to ease the extraction when the intestines are pulled out and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the tear of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is ruptured, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man hurt in the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and it was the wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was sewn up and became a fistula, and from there came vomiting and diarrhea.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him according to what I knew, and did not stop applying subtle treatments until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the sickness had come back in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no more harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced people said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be stitched up in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take thread of fine hemp, then gather together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has opened up the mouth, put it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that its mouth is closed together again;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cover the end, and it will hold so well that it cannot be undone.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another thread after it, in this manner as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This method has proved effective in the intestine, and brings no harm to the sick person.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if it is possible to sew the intestine with a thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take one end of this intestinal thread that has been thoroughly cleaned.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread a fine linen thread twisted into a thin cord.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and then pass it through the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with thread is no better than the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or healing, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes ulcerated, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it has healed and closed up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is, according to medical knowledge, a hard and white, or rather painless, nodule-like formation.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also healed like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts open and closes up again, and other times it becomes more swollen.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and other times large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the section on wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no scab,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but by one of the eight reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness or dryness of the blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its bad quality.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scab inside and on the lips that does not allow new scab to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much swelling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is foul and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine used in its treatment is not good.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption has turned into a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of its property in the region, digestion is slow and health is slow to come back, and it is inclined by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the treatments with medicine in the section on divisions.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is fitting that I inform you of the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and the arteries, and the nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the scabbard, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar wounds.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are difficult to heal, and there is no cure except labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the wound I have mentioned, and you have faith in its treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it to be known, take a thread of silver or iron, if the fistula is straight, tie it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, search for a fine thread of linen.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the linen thread bends easily around the twistiness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot clearly search it with threads,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one opening to another, and purifies.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then tie it off tightly as you are able, knowing whether there is bone or nerve inside and that it has healed thoroughly.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you about, then cover it up according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the corrupt flesh and scabs that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then heal it until it is completely healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deeply located in a right place, it is fitting that you cover it thoroughly as long as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put moist threads of medicated glue in the wound and insert them up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine dissolves the remaining excess at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply unguents of fresh scab as soon as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve injures or affects the principal member, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it until all the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal with new scab things as soon as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and returns to the previous state.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the bottom of this matter.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	so uncover and investigate until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot intervene.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy than to accept it as nature wills.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then extract them all, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture gets in the way and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cover it up with moisture and scab, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put on the wound something new to prevent putrefaction.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the place around the bones is foul and putrid.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the one in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone.
puis restoure la plaie;	and then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of it that comes close to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then you should scrape and cover it completely up to the corruption, and then heal it until it is closed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and assistance in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter came out to the leg and he was afflicted with a large abscess, without any external reason for it to break open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but through their foolishness they covered it up so much that the abscess burst open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings that all flowed with the foul liquid of the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians put remedies into it for two years, and there was no relief in the art of medicine.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called to it, and saw his leg and the remedies with which they were treating him.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed out through the openings had a large amount of pus.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red and had a yellowish (citrus-like) color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a thread into one of these openings, and then searched all the openings.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were all connected to each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hastened and covered one of the openings as far as I could until I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came up to the bone itself inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I believed that there was no other corruption, except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and then I began to restore the wound with healing medicines over a long period of time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I restarted, and re-exposed the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption continued in the bone, and I scraped it away, and then removed it, and I tried to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	But I am not able until I cover around a palm's length of bone, and the flesh heals to its full depth.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	Then I treated him with medicine; and he was healed and mended quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often there was bloody discharge due to evacuation, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contraindication from head to toe, nor to eat or to drink.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it must be set in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one and press it to the head of the bone that opens.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put one more thread of linen larger than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and expose the flesh on the place where you see it healing, so that it heals without bleeding.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot ember or a flat piece of wood under the bone to melt the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to heal as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and to heal again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so that you expose the flesh entirely; then put a hot ember underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then heal from one part to the other the corruption, and let it be the same size as the original corruption, as we have said before;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupted joint and heal the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then there is no remedy but to cut them off.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or in the thumb of the foot, then it is very serious.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you should ask that corroded place how it opens;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you can, but beware of the vein or nerve that might be against it.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and threads to cut those bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and according to their thickness and subtlety, their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary for each artisan to prepare his instrument according to the appearance of the work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the tool that you will need, according to your knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so that you think about the tool you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	from fire (presumably, this is a transition back to the original text, where "du feu" would indicate the use of heat in some way)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can be corrupted or spoiled because of something inside [the eye], or because of something outside [the eye].
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corruption with the remedy of medicines, and they do not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the disease may escape by cutting off death or the worse evil, which is the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness appears, then the corruption of the member spreads from member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and it takes hold throughout the body; so hasten to cut it off.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and a viper and similar things.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the eye, then cut it off, and do not give it a chance to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it off at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that's death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy stronger than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do just so when the corruption comes to the foot; if it comes in the first joint, cut off after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, then cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, then cut off at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or healing the member is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one servant downwards from one ligature, and another servant upwards from the other ligature.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you tear apart the flesh that is between the two ligatures by one wide spatula, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or heal it, and put a linen cloth on each side of it, so that the healing does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess comes to the sick person.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if there comes bleeding from the cut when you work, so cauterize the spot immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restrictive powders; then return to your medication until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured limb with a convenient bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to me, Iohn in the flesh:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a burn which seemed like coal of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that burning came first in his right foot, until it had consumed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the burn, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long time after that the burn came back on his right hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things repellent after purification of the body, and the burns could not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I had cut off his hand, he would have died,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtue of the man was weak; and he entirely lost hope, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then he hastened to cover his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not concealed this account, except for what is made in other lands, when it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At times an abscess comes to a fatty place and stays so long that it forms a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and opens up, and the pus jumps out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as delicate as a silk cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not spread to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "abscess" or "boil", but I think you mean to say that it is called "carbuncle".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it's not called a "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in depth, then it's called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so delicate that if you cut around it entirely, and similarly when it is as thin as a silk cloth,
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	it will not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with fat, then scrape it with a lancet thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breast is large, and the abscess that comes from it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then lance it with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take assafoetida, oil, and litarre (litarge), equally, and put the skin in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	so that the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and make it into water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and lance the breast with it, and stop up the hole.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay in for two hours, then extract it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is purified and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at any time it is lanced with ashes' water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take the ashes of a vine's trunk, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and lance with it, until you know that the breast is well purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the illness cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes' water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then lance with honeyed water and a bit of powdered litarre mixed in.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you lance it with honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property to purify and cleanse.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then lance with it so that flesh grows in there.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and then take diaphinite plaster and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you lance with various medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said or which treat ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the hole of the breast is small, and the lancet of the lance cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with a needle a little bit, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave just one hole or opening where the lancet can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the hole that empties pus is on top, then cut it down to the lowest part of the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is deep in, it doesn't let flesh grow.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the breast below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then sew it up in such a way that the pus drains to the lowest part of the wound.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the pus is deep inside, it doesn't let flesh grow.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the breast below as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then sew it up in such a way that the pus runs down easily and leaves no pus.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and then place a linen cloth over it that covers the entire breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at a strong point near the hole of the breast, one spot larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply sweet ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it over the wound of the breast to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth outside for at least a few days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the wound of the breast, take it off often to empty out the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of the pus, whether it is venom or much or enough, digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there are ulcers or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has extended in this manner and you see the nature that comes up on the wound of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is already healing, and approach the patient's cure.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then let him loose in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast empties out undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom flows for a long time afterward, do not despair of its health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the cure approaches. For there are men whose flesh is slow to grow in their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and becomes putrid, then add medicinal substances that are moist in nature but dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphinite ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and that is the final medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphinite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and equal parts of old vinegar in substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same with thickened cooked honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphinite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and pound them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then pour this mixture into a cloth, and place it on the breast, and do not administer anything else to it for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of heaven, which is also like flour of cypress and century plant.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them as simples or composites: pound them and make powder, and mix with the honey that I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made impression in the bone, or hard members, or sinews.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so treat it with the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the ulcer or sore on the inguen (groin).
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pannarium is an ulcer that forms in the groin of the pouch of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps it forms in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and allowed to become old, a hot ulcer comes.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they flow and empty pus as long as the root of the ulcer flows, and perhaps it drains all of it.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes a corruption just to the bone, so that there is a stinking pain, and the leg of the foot is swollen, and the color is full of flux.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut off the entire surplus of flesh that remains from the ulcer.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy and the ulcer is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the ulcer starts to eat away at the flesh, begins to gangrene, and becomes putrid,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a thread of linen under the ulcer that is eating away at the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tightly, and cut out the fine and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has reached the bone, then cut it out and treat the wound, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the bone becoming corrupted, then cut it out with a knife in one piece, as has been said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and hurts a lot, then it's necessary to lance it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the ulcer on the swelling with a crosswise incision above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not reach as far as the flesh under the ulcer, for the patient would feel a lot of pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The wrist joint that forms in some men's hands, perhaps it is all fatty.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps there is a joint or a bone in it, and never an ulcer.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them occur at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the bones of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that form in any of the joints of the hand do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that form at the joint of the wrist, perhaps it can move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is fatty will be light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that form in the root of the joint are grievous to cure, and you should hold back from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that which forms in or at the last joint, it is necessary to cut out the surrounding flesh up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut out the bone with a suitable thread, and treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The burn that comes on the hand together comes by birth, or by a blow of a wound, or by being burned with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out the burn, so that the joint can be repaired according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloth moistened in rose oil, so that they do not become scarred.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is healed, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If burn comes on any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that burn as it is necessary.
Des vils	The wounds that come from a fall or an accident.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are swollen and inflamed, filled with melancholic excess fluids, that come in many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to them no purging of choler, and then heal the wound with basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure by iron is according to two manners: one is to cut them and treat the wound with fire and black salve.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you cover the wound, and let it dry out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut is according to this manner: first heat the leg with hot water very strongly, until the big vein becomes subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the leg of the sick person from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the wound in one place, or in two places, or in three places, with a wide incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then clean and treat with fire the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the sick person can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it up and order him to eat meat that brings out black choler.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and the healing when the wounds are full and cause harm to the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The shaving of the leg is according to this manner: shave the leg of the sick person, if there is a lot of hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and inflame the wounds.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat him with fire, and then cut the place of the wound in length from the top of the kneecap to the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with hot iron and flay the wound from each side, until it appears when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems as white as a cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put thread under it, until it is raised from the skin, and then sew it with a light touch.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place above the three fingers, and flay the skin over the wound until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then sew it up with thread, as you have done before, and sew it to another needle, as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if needed, then sew it up and cut the skin at the foot's joint.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then treat and lift up to the second incision, then pull it from one incision to another, until it all comes out completely, and then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it up, then insert a needle into each thread with a strong double point.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and sew and treat it, and insert the needle under one thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it all comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut through, because if it cuts through, then it cannot be pulled out or lifted up, and will cause harm to the sick person.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and once you have treated it completely, put moistened wool on the wound with wine and rose oil, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the flesh of the wound is contracted, twisted, and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	it is necessary to cut through it crookedly, but do not cut all the way through; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the flesh is curved, and does not cut through, so that it cuts only the wound.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a thick curvature, because if it were thin, it would cut through the wound; but be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	The civil wound.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This wound is dry in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in earth that has little moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it occurs in other places than the legs, and these come from the corruption that comes under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as when it comes from worms and serpents inside the body, being dry between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that it comes to the leg with a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the wound begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens up, it is necessary to wrap around a strip of linen from one and a half fingers to two and a half fingers, and tie it with a knot.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth hanging at the leg, and every time it becomes moist again, wrap around the cloth and tie the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap around the remaining part, but do not cut through to its root until it has come out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about an ulcer or corruption in the place, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of this thing it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the head, and nothing remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this wound when treated is as long as five or ten palms.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it came out from ten palms in length, and when you cut it, the thread or cord comes out as far as its bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and so everything comes out, and the material that was inside becomes empty, and you administer to the place medicine that brings out corruption each day, then treat it as for ulcers.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this wound has many veins, and especially when it opens up at the joint of the foot or in the foot itself.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes to pass that it bursts forth with pus, and from which there pours blood; then heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of an ox" because it happens many times to oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels very painful when it moves from member to member, so much that the skin splits where it goes and pours out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is a corruption of bad humors, such as come from worms and serpents and lice and ascarides or belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and we doubt its wickedness because when it goes through the body, it climbs to the head and comes into the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it enters in and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him heal and remove it, one cannot do any better than when he goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong string tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then sew over it and remove the thread, and if the worm is deeply in the flesh and you can't find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so cauterize it with fire on top until it chars.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it infects the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see him coming close to the head near the eye, you must tie a thread under it tightly, then sew over it and remove the thread.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the sick person in purging of body with dissolvent medicines for the corrupting bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and they should avoid strong meats that cause corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain members.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I have seen those things that I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the inner part of the upper arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and not long afterwards, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, just like quick silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while later it ran through the whole body, so much so that it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body all the time, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness move in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen that the pain would move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it move like this, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a sick body and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason the windiness appeared to be constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in those who are robust and have moist bodies and veins that are well-replenished.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see cure this illness, and the sick person feels that pain, if she tells you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	so bind her above and below hastily, then sew over it until the windiness has been constrained at that place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you cannot see it to your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then use remedies that drive out the windiness, such as bitter pills and serpent's pills and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrowroot (a type of medicinal herb)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The types of arrowroot are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they occur.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those which have great points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and soldered ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with horns, and those that have pieces or fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which grows in any member grows in two ways: either it grows into the principal member, growing out like a horn,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it grows in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you about next, become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so beware of the extraction of this arrowroot, for death comes afterwards in various ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if you do not see this bad sign and the arrowroot is not deeply inside, then pull it out and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrowroot pierces it and makes a hole in the bone, and leaps out the sphenoid bone which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when you have blindness and dullness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it leads to swelling of the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is discharge from the wound of moist white pus, resembling powder, and it also comes out like charcoal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see these signs, then take care of the treatment, and pull out the arrowroot if it is not in too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrowroot when it pierces the heart are that it is close to the left nipple, and feels like it has been stuck into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrowroot moves in the same way as pus, and flows with black blood, and comes out cold and frosty sweat, and causes fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then you must be aware without a doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowroot when it never leaves the spleen is that foam comes out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient turns blue, and gasps loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowroot pierces the covering of the spleen, it is located near the lower ribs; and there is a great pain and a great distress and gasping; and all the muscles of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowroot pierces the stomach, perhaps something indigestible comes out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowroot pierces the abdomen and comes out through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrowroot.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowroot pierces the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows away, and the patient feels a great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and hips and knees and calves and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrowroot is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one of my friends who had an arrowroot in his arm near the elbow joint.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled it out from a different angle under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrowroot from a child that had been in the fat of the eyelid, near the eyebrow.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrowroot was swollen and I could only grasp the tip towards the eye socket.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrowroot was as big as a Turkish bowstring, with the whole iron tip without ears; the child was healed and did not experience any bad aftermath.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrowroot from a Christian's throat, and it was the Arabic type with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shave the hairs, and I make them fine until they are drawn out, and the Christian is bled.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I draw an arrow, i.e. to one's home, which was stuck in his belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow and pulled it out, and it went out without any bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whom an arrow struck in the back, and the wound was sewn up on top;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow stayed inside him, and did not change his natural disposition;
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and thus remained without great suffering, and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I draw an arrow at one of the king's princes, which was stuck in his neck.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was somewhat leaning to the right side, and the arrow was completely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the care after it had been stuck for three days. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched around with all a subtle tent, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and hurt under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow;
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on him a poultice attractive and digestive, so that the place would not become inflamed.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the place of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on him the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the sick person remained healthy for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow's presence for one day inside his neck; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a caustic medicine for many days, so that it became open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was corroding at the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that caustic medicine, so that the tip of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the end was well healed around four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then it erupted so that I stuck in the forceps on both sides and it couldn't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I didn't stop from probing and inventing ways with instruments, until I got it one day with well-made forceps.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, as much as I was able to do, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sutured and the sick person was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can put your treatment on what I don't say, because books cannot take in everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compound well with a small quantity of things, and on what is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have found nine works, and nine instruments, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I will translate the text exactly as requested.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps over it to get in on the other side is its socket entering into the fleshy parts, and jumping over each time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, then let it be left alone until the flesh is quite purulent around it, and the exit is cleared out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it has set in the bone, and it cannot come out, then let it be left thus for some days, and let it move each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it does not, then let a fine needle be inserted all the way through, until the surrounding place is widened, and then let it be pulled.
