Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the socket has set into the bone of the head, and goes right up to one of the hemispheres of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and any of the accidents that I said would appear to the patient: if it does not come out, but is left thus for some days;
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the splinter comes up as far as the skin, that's the dead one.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the splinter is not set into anything but the bone alone, and does not come up to the skin,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains in the patient for some days without any bad accident, then it is a sign that the splinter can be drawn out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very tightly set in and cannot come out that way, then I administer tar to the area, as I told you before. Then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the splinter has been pushed back into the flesh of the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it in its entirety under the tent;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with some suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the splinter,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then enlarge the wound so that it is wide.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the splinter if you can, and if there are ears on the splinter with which it holds in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut away the flesh that is stuck to both parts of the splinter as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the splinter so that you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the splinter, for then you would have to pull it out more roughly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then let it be until the flesh around the wound has grown over and covered it, then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding does not stop, administer what we have said about treating it in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and think up a plan how you can draw out the splinter without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either soon or late, either strongly or gently, and put the patient back in the form he was in when the splinter fell into him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest help to be done, and if you cannot, then put him back according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The splinter that comes out from another place, or if it pierces any part of the body, or if the skin is swollen and inflamed in the area where it can be seen or felt clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut above it, so that the tweezers can take hold of it, and then draw it out. And if it jumps out now,
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand around strongly, so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then resume drawing it out until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the handle of the splinter is remaining, then push it all the way back into the handle.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the handle slips out and you see that you need to administer binding, then apply one instrument with a pointed end.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the splinter enters into the hair of the instrument, and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the splinter is stuck, then insert one instrument with an entering point into it to ease out the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the splinter is embedded, it is advisable that you remove all the flesh around where the venom is, as far as you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound according to what is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the splinter has gone into the leg or arm or stomach or bladder or intestines and it is nearby, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then draw it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and heal as long as the wound is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which one treats splinters are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and small ones, according to the size of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the pointed end is also like a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	so that one can push it into the point of the splinter, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tweezers for pushing and checking if it fits like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one bleeds are 31, and of these 16 have a head or origin.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two jugular veins which are behind the ears, and are called "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in two visible temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, and are called "spiracles".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins which are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and they are called "labial veins".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one bleeds commonly are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "brachial", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the femoral.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that bleeds, which opens clearly above the pubic region.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvadore vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the curve of the left thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "popliteal" which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the bleeding, as I said to you, are that you raise the head of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a strap, or vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two small pouches of the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then take them with your thumb and press on the pulse below your thumb, so that it is more pronounced.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and push it under the vein just up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up to hold the vein in place.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and let out the blood and the vein well on both sides of the traveler, and make it bleed until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then close and tie it, so that it is sound again.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for old migraines.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and soderitis, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the core of the sharp tears in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bleeding are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens his neck, so that the two veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then press to make it more pronounced.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the skin over the vein upwards to your index finger, and push the lancet under it.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards and cut it, just like you did with the other two veins, and let out blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger on top of the vein for an hour, then apply a compress of cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then tie the form back up and let it be until it is sound again. And now I have spoken of both its cutting and extraction, which were at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is worth just as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases, and for migraines, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient tightens his neck in a twisting motion, so that the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossoir", and whose shape is this: (description of an instrument)
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press upwards with your hand or another object, and let out blood according to how much you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck and tie the vein so that it is sound again, and in no case make a wide incision.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not advisable to make the incisions too sharp, and to bleed across, because the bone is close by, and there is a risk of breaking through the incision if it is too delicate.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the corners of the eyes helps with eye diseases, and with conjunctivitis, and with redness, and with iridocyclitis in the eye, and with face diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck in twisting motion, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it bleed, and make the incision of the traveler be a little long and a little wide, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the incision is delicate, it may break through; then make the bleeding stop, as much as you need to, and then tie with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding from the vein of the nose is worth for ague, and for severe sore throat, and for face diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that come to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then compresses his nose with his left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the delicate incision long and place it between the two nostrils, in the space that is between the nose's wings.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well here, and the bleeding will now start to stop.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it go too far inside, and make the bleeding stop according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the incision: (description of an instrument or a shape)
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding from the two jugular veins helps with constriction of the arteries, and with inflammation, and with many diseases, and with epilepsy, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and with erythematos.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck on one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be sitting above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then make the incision on the vein long a little bit wide, then stop the bleeding temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat on the other vein, then release the ligature, and compress both veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle, and leave it until morning, so that the wound is sound again.
De la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding from the veins above the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and redness around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you, and compress their neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip upwards and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by their black color, and by the fine black veins surrounding them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut both of them, and if you are not sure, or in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one on each side, and do likewise with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	The bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding from the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for mouth diseases, and for eye diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks down on each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then cut both of them, but do not go too deep, because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the throat that we commonly bleed from are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by making a large incision in one spot, or a small and delicate incision like a surgeon's cut, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the incision is very well known, and it is wide as you see: (description of an instrument or a shape)
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to open the thick and bloody veins that contain much blood and are turbulent.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the incision "olivaire".
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate and pointed, and is for bleeding thin veins where the blood is very clear.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding from the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed carefully, and to beware of the artery that is under it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding from it comes out, then he needs to cauterize it, as I said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the incision should not be cut too deep, but rather trimmed like an "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, it is necessary to compress it and switch to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you can let go of it or bleed on the place where it is located in the arm instead, and it will appear clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut it with the incision "anesil", as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see where the bleeding is coming from, it is then necessary to compress the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then press on the spot to make it more pronounced, then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the incision "anesil".
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not touch the artery when you see the spot swollen, because it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	quickly then, and place your finger on top for a long time, and remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then tie the arm and leave it so, and do not move the patient until they are sound again. And be on guard, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and you are in a hurry, and medical treatment is not available, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will retreat, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of plantain bark, split it in half, and tie one half on top tightly until the other day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	And if the bleeding stops, that's well; and if not, then apply the powders that stop blood, as we have said.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not affected by many conditions for small wound and strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps to stop blood from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the bleeder to beware of the nerve that is under, and if he cuts too deep, and finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the wound becomes inflamed, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you should bleed from the instrument "anesil", and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding from the cephalic vein helps to stop blood from the head, and is useful for them.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by making an incision with the olive-shaped knife or the mercurial knife, because it is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerve or artery under it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Toutevoie, it becomes necessary to find the most suitable position, and do not worry if one fails at first, and try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, the joints swell in some people when one fails to reset it the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about healing, is that healing comes easily only by preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and in order to prevent diseases from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the healing should be done in one of the three ways that are hot or cold: to wit, head heat, fasting, and warm bathing;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should heal oneself in the early days of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should heal oneself on the first day or the third, after 2 hours or 3 double days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing which is administered for diseases has no appointed time, but when necessity calls by day or night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not fitting to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor women who are pregnant for more than a quarter of the month until the seventh;
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly be healed who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be healed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light purge.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there are many foul things retained, so that the vessels do not draw out the superfluities from the intestines, which are harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal who is too fat with meats, or drunk, as long as they remain so, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and it is worse to try to heal after being seized by colic, vomiting, and diarrhea of the belly, and excessive activity with women, labor, watching and fasting, and all that exhausts virtue, either through something related to war or the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the body is thick, with meats and drinks and medications, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then bathe or take a warm bath, unless something prevents it, to subtlety purify the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal yourself with wine around the third part of the belly, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be happy and joyful, and let the healer be more superior than the one who is healed, and slap him on the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and take care of the connection above in a moderate way, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the body.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub him with the fingers of the hand, so that the veins become swollen and one can feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	and then moisten the healer with a small flame of old oil, and put his thumb of his left hand on top of the vein where he wants to heal.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not flow and spill at the moment of piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings when being healed, and some such as are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when you put the flame on it, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it overflows the vein, it means the wound is too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the healer be knowledgeable in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein overflows the first time, it is good; but if not, then he should start again a little below or above that place, unless the skin is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the skin is swollen and the patient is afraid, then let him leave it alone for one or two days, and do not tie up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps a boil will form there; do not take a bath, then start to heal it again if you please.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the hole is small, or the body bleeds subtly and you doubt that it does not bleed as much blood as you see, then pierce into that same hole with all the flame straightly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and do it hastily, so that the skin is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the skin swollen, do not start to heal it again, and put a little linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and is nourishing in this place where the oil is mixed with the lard.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil in each healing of veins that you perform, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done with vinegar and wine, when it is put on the place; for it subtlety stops the blood and sets it apart when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a big boil comes up, which happens many times, especially when the wound is not well healed again at that same time or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and put a wet sponge on the place in hot water and vinegar for a short time, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if after some days there is no blackening or greenish color at the place, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see fit, apply something made with aloes or myrrh mixed in a liquor of camphor, mastich, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of badness in the healing of the basilica (a type of wound or swelling), then put your hand on it, and if you find that the place feels soft to the compression of the hand, then it is a sign of badness.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to put any of the things we have said on it, for perhaps it will cut off blood from an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And consider each type of blood according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the blood is black, let it flow out until it turns red; and if it looks thick, let it be thinned out; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the person who is swollen and sore, and in need of bloodletting, that you make a larger incision, and be careful not to cut too deeply.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the person who is weak, you should do the opposite, and strive to make them whole quickly, and they must be healed by cutting across, not in a piercing manner.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of healing is safe from the corruption of blood and the crushing of nerves, and it is worth more than a long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the person whose body is failing in healing, it is necessary to give them a moist compress soaked in juice of seeded pomegranates; if they are overheated, draw blood 3 or 4 times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold complexion, mix before the healing moist compress with honey syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they have bad breath after healing, after the flow of blood is stopped, it is necessary that they smell broth made from meat and a fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and follow the other things we have said in the chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of vomit.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bloodletting, that he let the body recover a little bit at a time, according to the quantity of his strength continuing.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to straighten his arm after the first bloodletting and he has a strong pulse, will recover in 7 hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be bled on another occasion, must be bled the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood within the body that is already heated up and brings on fever; thus it is necessary to draw out a great quantity and to enlarge the puncture as far as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you warn all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand on his pulse when it bleeds, lest the morbid condition come in place of purgation.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and such things happen many times, when the bloodletting is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not happen when you wish to untie the arm and let out blood the second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press strongly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, should he stretch his arm hastily, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him leave it until he bleeds the second time; or you have reached the tip of the flame with your needle, so that the blood which has frozen at the puncture comes out freely.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on .i. pot of warm oil and press on it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let him leave it alone and not bind it at all, until the inflammation has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to let out blood the second time, then he should bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled instead of that of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bleeding is such that the sick person dips their hand in hot water until the skin is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be tied lightly, so that the vein appears well, then he should bleed now from across, not from the length or the width.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the puncture be wide, and let it bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then dip the hand in hot water again, and leave the blood to congeal in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's winter, do not dip the hand in hot water again, for one lets it go further into winter than into summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding of this vein is more safe from all other veins, which have arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the cubital vein of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is evacuated, so that we can see;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the finger is crooked, and you cut off all the skin from top to bottom, it should not hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep because the nerves are under all the skin denuded of flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have taken out as much blood as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and thread to sew it up quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding from the hand of the left side is worth the disease of the madmen, and do everything in the same way as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The bleeding from the forehead is worth all the diseases that are under the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as ailments of the marrow, and retention of fluids, and disease of the reins, and the hips, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his bleeding is that the sick person puts their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the foot, and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot they go out many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	bleed the one that is the largest vein, or the one at the ankle, which I value more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut into the vein on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut through them also as in cutting; and be careful with the flaps.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the swelling cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well of the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the poultice fails the first time, then start again the second time higher up a spot, for the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	don't doubt about nerves, as we have said, and do similarly with the swelling of the other foot also.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the knee of fear, and its swelling amounts to the pain of the haunch, when it is by hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its swelling is that the patient goes between bath and bed, and stretches above the knee 4 fingers in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open up; and if it does open, then you should let it drain in all ways that you can, and cutting across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth trying to cut into it, for the wound is salty, and it has been swollen for many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you can't find the vein, then drain any that opens up or at the back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and drain out as much blood as you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on some cotton and bind it up; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	The remedies for a poultice.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or iron, or glass; and the application of leeches is done in two ways: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this leeching which is done without piercing is in two ways: either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the leeching which is done by piercing and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	where one is at the top of the head, and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more on both sides of the neck, and the leech under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the leeches on the shoulders, and the leech above the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the leeches in both arms, and the leeches in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches on the two ankles; and the leeching does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it has no strength at all, just like bleeding from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable for administration, either with fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from overfilling, until the entire body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases or by habit, we must bleed, then let us administer each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between, and in each season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they need to bleed, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who findpletion and darkness in their face, and head, and neck, and eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit up blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who have nightmares, and see through their blood and wounds and bites and like-like things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and all the more so when it's in the middle of the month, let us order to bleed after three hours of day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the nose helps in the relief of the headache... that comes to the eyes, and it is not suitable that this should be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bleeding is in place of the nasal blood-letting.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not suitable for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because this does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and on account of this, it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, and on this account it is necessary to place the leech a little lower by reason of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The bleeding in the neck is in place of blood-letting from the head and the vertebrae, and on this account it is worth the constriction of the stomach.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for obstruction of the channel of the womb, and for stoutness, and for overfilling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be a little forced, because if it is too tightly held, it causes forgetfulness or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The bleedings from the two sides of the neck are worth for headaches, and eye pains, and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pains in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of blood-letting from the vertebrae; and let you command the leecher that he should express his hand to put, that he does not cut the artery, and do not come back with great blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The bleedings under the chin are worth for mouth diseases and corruption of gums and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of blood-lettings from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bleedings under the armpits are worth for diseases that come from heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The bleedings of the hips are worth as much as the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it attracts blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the leecher that he does not pierce too deeply there, because the place is bare of flesh and lies next to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is above the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath, and it is necessary that the leech be big and made of iron, so that it can suck well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs bleed openly, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and they clean out the flowers; and they replace the two saphene veins and the two ankle veins, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and make a person more susceptible to fainting in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the leech is to put it on first empty, and let it suck in a timely manner, and then place it hastily, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redder of the blood; then pierce, and replace the leeches, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are such people who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice with only one prick.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we repeat the pricking often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce deeply, and the ends are such that the veins should be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the leeches with an oily, dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is with camphor oil, or violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is with oil of ivy, or plantain oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the residue is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who is being bled has tender flesh and wide pores, there should be no need to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very damp, should rise with ease, or rose water, and myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick residues should rise with old wine, or vinegar of oak, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to bleed with a leech before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the bleeding.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be warned, when he must be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take heed of those who bleed are choleric, and the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	for it is necessary that he take cold things, such as green apples, endives, and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mild pottage, and the flesh of chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and moderately scented wine, which is between old and new, and mild pottage, and mild pottage, and small game birds and chickens.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day on which he will be bled, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people some time three times or muscatel wine before the bleeding, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are applied without piercing are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the loin, because those members cannot tolerate being pierced above.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we place on the shoulders when the disease is bleeding; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as we place leeches on the belly and navel to reduce the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain, when there is swelling or abscess; and perhaps its attractive virtue can break the swelling, or draw out the abscess from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and it does this when it is placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained bloodiness.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these leeches are administered empty to suck only, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of vinegar.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in the disease of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the leech with hot water only, or with water in which herbs have been cooked that are suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the leech administered with fire is such:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers of length and a half palm deep, and on the outside around the middle there should be one small pith, as to hold an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of linen, smooth on the front so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle there should be a rod of iron or steel crossed over to hold a candle in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there should be great and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the cups for children are different from those of adults, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus put this cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	hold the candle of wax or a linen wick, and put it in the cup across the rod that is inside the cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light be at the bottom of the cup so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and the two ends should be over the pith that we said, so that when one wants to, the steam goes out, and take off the cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and use the linen wick again if needed, and reapply it often, as you may need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cup for phrensy that is administered in acute illness, there is no rod nor pith, and it is only administered when it is full of water, and is put on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	nor are they administered forcibly except in members where one cannot put cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on bare skin devoid of fat, such as the neck or elbow, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cups that are in sweet and clear waters without sediment, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in fresh water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be rinsed with vinegar and cupping vessel, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the cups.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and bulging, if it is a place where one can put a cup, then put them there, because this will work much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift up the limb and then dry it well, and then apply the cup.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too hot after taking off the cups, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and put it on, until the heat has gone away.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the pain is intense, put on vinegar that has been boiled or gallstones and similar things, until it is cooled down.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put on the limb half of peeled peas, and leave them until they are warm against the skin, which will now cool down.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other cups.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the cups cannot be taken, rub the limb with fresh blood or prick it with a needle until the cup lets go.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will heat up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bubbling, sprinkle on a bit of burnt aloes and linen, or ashes, and they will now burst.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a restoration of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Be aware, dear son, that foolish people will look at this chapter and see nothing of the ancient books, nor read any letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is estranged the science in our land, for I never found a good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except by the knowledge of the ancient books which I have studied so much that I have treated the science and by experience and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained and shortened at the end and shown clearly the forms of instruments which are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book the contents and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding and remains on virtue, so that those who have been proven know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that whenever break or dislocation or torsion or fracture comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person, first and foremost, unless some other thing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of body, or pregnancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the flesh is very cold or too hot; and beware of choleric fever, that is to say cold sweats, and the flesh of bird and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any greasy meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot aposteme or spreading of matter in the member; then revigorate the sick person to their primary government as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to recover, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with meats that make thick nourishment or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and cheese, and bread, and bacon, and eggs, and fresh fat fish, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the bones repair themselves more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well repaired or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those either who are too fragile, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But there is no cure, scrape off the broken bone, that is to say thick scabs which have formed and join the member together, as long as it grows back as it was before; and do not take away his labor, and therefore it must be nourished with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the back or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur to the radius, and others in twisting, such as the break of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with a small split or crack all the way through.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own remedy and proper instrument in the restoration, according to how the memory comes to it.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and a fracture of the bone is known by what causes the joint to twist and opens well from outside, and sounds like a hollow when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if there is no twisting or sound on pressing, and the sick person does not feel great pain, then it is not a fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or cracking, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move the joint with the hand, but apply medicines that will come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that is in twisting and where the two parts are separated, it must now be put into place equally, so that hot apostemes do not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot apostemes come, let him leave them alone for a day, until the apostemes are calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it in place again with a bandage that you can apply lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of the one who has fragments. then bind it, as must be done later.
