Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken fragments, and you can pull apart two parts, whether it's hand or foot, or if at your hand it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and with your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, scrape away with all remedies the additions in their place with a bandage that you can apply, and take care that by your work no lesion or pain comes to the sick person.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join together the two ends of the bone in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if you think it's not well, feel with your hand and straighten it gently, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring by their work hot apostemes and contractions to the member, which we have warned of many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, scold the patient well so that he does not move it, nor while watching or sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it must be put in such a condition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is set straightly, so that twisting does not come when it has been restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as fingers and toes and hands: they must be enveloped in soft and subtle linen wraps.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: they must be enveloped in a wide and sturdy linen bandage, because the large bands embrace all the great member and bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no unevenness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie the ends of the bandage loosely, three or four turns according to the member, and bind your hand at one end of the bandage, then go up to the fracture and bind it less tightly than the fracture, so that the fracture will be a little farther away from the binding.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little and a little more, until you take up most of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage and wind it around again on top of the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the fracture and bind it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages strips of linen or cloth, so that they are all even, then tie everything together with one bandage, and then put your well-made pads on top, if there is no swelling or effusion.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or hot aposteme, put on something soothing that will calm the heat and remove the swelling, and let it be for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind over your pads with something of the same width as a well-made cord or thong, or of the wood from which we make knives, or of palm strips, and be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the pad that you put over the fracture is a little larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it needs to be for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind over the pads in the same way that you did in the first chapter, then tie above with a thread loosely, as you did above the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is above, the looser below; and it must be that the thread is moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are too thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bandages with linen strings twisted tight, and it is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it must not have less than two fingers' width between each pad.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is scratched by the threads of the pads after they have been tied on in their healthy places, he should put under them strips of linen or chopped fleece so that he does not get hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is together with the fracture and the nerves are broken, I will say the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind all the broken members with pads on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put strong pads on them before five or seven days, or more according to your security in avoiding hot swelling.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient ointments for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is held against the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this concoction in a way that is not too clear nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common manner of the ointment that restores the fracture to many dispositions, and especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of ointment restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take 30 aloe, and ladani, and enule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and myrrh, each 10; myrrh and aloes, each 5; alechil, 8. And make them into powder, and mix with plenty of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this ointment, for it has a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for torsions: take myrrh and valerian root, each 10; myrrh and aloes, each 8; asafoetida, 6; Armenian balm, 10. And crush them well, and mix with egg or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of ointment for joints and broken bones that are separated from their place, and soothes the pain that accompanies them, and is used to dress the wound: take new linen, and moisten it in warm oil and in soft ashes, and put it on the place. This ointment does not heal, but it is good to calm hot swelling, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment that heals broken bones: take dry leaves of fig tree and leaves of terrestrial plantain, and crush them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of ointment for the restoration of bone fracture and to reduce remaining swelling. Take root of valerian, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and crush them, and mix with wine, and if the member is hot, mix it with moisted coriander water or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of ointment that is stronger than the first one, when hard swelling comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of valerian, and seeds of flax, balm, melilotus, and absinthe, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and crush them, and mix with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says that the ointment to be put on a broken member in order to restore it strongly is nothing other than cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on a broken member in order to restore it, things that are slightly warm and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of ointment that is good for lesions and pain: take myrrh and chopped men's hair or bird quills, and valerian root, and equal parts, and crush them, and make an ointment with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen the bandage a little after that, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone returned to its place, do not remove the bandage for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or swelling, with rest or effusion, then hasten and remove the bandage, and take off the ointment now; and take a light cloth and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift up the place, as long as the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a knot, as long as you are sure of avoiding hot swelling.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member be calmed down and the pain be gone, then start again with a fine bandage and a little ointment, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and do this in a subtle way until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and effusion have been completely eliminated, and you need ointment and bandages again, then restart it, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not remove the bandage until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and sometimes leave it for as long as 20 days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals and approaches the joining of the bone with flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then bind the member more tightly than before, and let the flesh grow back, as I said before. And if you see that the place is drying out more than necessary, know that there will be no new growth.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then take a mixture of hot water and vinegar every time you remove the bandage, and do it once every three days, and wash out some of the ointment.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, therefore, the scarring is reduced on the member, and healing is accelerated of what foolish people do to restore the member improperly: it is bad, and it is a fearful task, and I see nothing but laziness and doing things incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems that we have reached the end of the text, which appears to be a medieval medical treatise on various types of bone fractures and their treatment.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of breaks are, and various forms, and the causes are specified;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breaks caused by the striking of a sword, and the arm crushes all the bone just up to the syphac which is under the bone, as happens with an axe or fist; and for that reason this kind of break is called "hacheure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and this kind of break is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two breaks is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact driven in, or a split, or a blow with a stone fist, or falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a pressing break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed in with the bone as subtle as a hair, and it is a small split, and for that reason this break is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone or by falling, or by something similar, and it makes the bone piece go inwards, and there is a hole left like when a blacksmith heats things up on the cauldrons; if iron goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And it happens more often in those who have or have had soft bones, like an infant's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens with all these kinds of breaks in which small pieces are broken off, like that; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the kinds of breaks by the description above them, and the investigation that has been done, and through the spoiled flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently with a finger, if the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful about the bad accidents that can happen to the patient. And if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, paralysis, feverishness, and the eyes coming out red and inflamed, and other similar symptoms in more severe conditions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightful accidents and you hope for recovery, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first and it's in winter, it is advisable to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane under the bone doesn't become corrupted, and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, it is advisable that you split the broken part thus: and have someone hold the patient's head hurt, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound as smoothly as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if hemorrhaging comes to expose the bone, or a boil appears, then the patient needs help, and it is that you fill the place with dampened cloths in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the boil is calmed down and there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and it's done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut at a narrow incision from front to back, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions of different widths, some narrow and others wide, with points of iron indented, and work lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer incisions with awls, not too deep that they do not penetrate through the head of the bone; and there should be above the point a margin or a circle, that does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each one goes in its place on the edge of the bone, so that you have awls for all the head; and this is the shape of the three ways of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one awl on the bone and turn it back and forth until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then put the awl in a different place a little later, and do this all around, then cut with the forceps the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do it as subtly and lightly as possible, just as we have said, so that you can extract the bone with your hand or with any of the instruments that you have such as tweezers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you scrape off the sharpness that remains of the bone from any other instrument resembling a forceps, but it needs to be sharper and more subtle than the other forceps;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, then scrape them off lightly with one of the instruments; then heal the wound with threads and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of surgery that Galen says is more sure; and he speaks very highly of it, and it is his own word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break is most apparent, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incision [the instrument], in whose form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the parts are sharp on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you lightly chop all around the bone, and be careful of the membrane that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it adheres to the bone, then lightly scrape it off, because one scrapes it off without much harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not penetrate as far as the membrane, and the bone is chopped so only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to cover that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle rasp which you should have in various quantities, so that you can use them in each place where it seems most convenient, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rub with coarse rasps, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and fine breaks, it is necessary that you smooth out according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be attributed to someone who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, then it is necessary that you take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another linen cloth, double in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you don't irritate the skin, then apply above one other linen and don't stretch it too much until it barely covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it be like this for one day or two, until the abscess has been calmed down, then remove it and administer remedies such as lily roots, and flax flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make powder from these things and apply them to the wound, and administer medicines that are not painful without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and take care that the wound is thoroughly clean, so you don't leave any ointment in it, nor let a bandage assemble over the skin of the brain, for when a bandage assembles over the cloth of the brain, they rot and putrefy, and cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is put on top of it, it becomes necrotic.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no worse condition comes to it than because of the medicine that has been put on it, and such virtue as it has, it is necessary for you to take a part of honey, and three parts of rosated oil and mix one cloth with it and place it on the wound;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the cure in ways of treatments that are necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that when the two parts of the nose above are broken or one by itself, for they are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous and does not break, so it does not cause more harm to bind or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary for you to set your little finger or a probe into the nose and push that breakage down into your index finger, and then put a poultice on the outside, until the nose recovers according to its natural figure.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and cannot be reached by the probe, it is necessary for you to put a small cork or plug there at the head of a reed, about a finger thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the breakage is in two parts, do it again in that way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not [on the first day], then after seven or ten days, when the swelling has gone down, then bind at the head of the nose with a cloth of linen, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side if it is there; and let the cloths be so thick that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers said that one should moisten the cloths with butter and change them each day. It doesn't seem to me to be a good thing, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the making of an egg custard and miller's powder; then leave the cloth, until the bone is hard and the cartilage has hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at times one places an oven or goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is .i. [one] sheet around it, and the patient holds the breath, and blows the patient through; therefore make the hole that you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to a boil while you are doing it, then put linseed oil or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in one pod of dragon's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the swelling does not come to a boil, then put an ointment on it from outside, of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with cooked egg yolk, then place light candles on top and do not bind the night.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break in the night is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then take it to suitable instruments, then sew the crack, and care for things that bring forth flesh, and soldering, as plasterings and ointments suitable to this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the night, then care for tents, and I put cloths of linen until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is broken beneath and there is no wound outside, and the break is outside only so slightly, and it is not broken in two, rather bent inward, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you press your middle finger into the mouth of the sick person; and if the break is on the left jaw, then press your middle finger of the right hand, and press the break inward lightly, and shape it with the other hand from outside, and set it equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the lower jaw is spread in two parts, it is necessary that you provide an extension of two parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth has happened or breaking, then pull them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw wax, and on one double cloth; and put on the cloth a strong strap well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth that you can, and command the sick person to rest, and give them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the face changes, then release it on the third day, and then reattach what has changed; and put a plaster on, of flour dust with plenty of egg or linseed meal, after you have removed the wax; and put on a light linen cloth, and if the plaster dries and the condition of the sick person does not change, leave it alone until it is healed. Many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling appears, administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it is a break and wound together, reward no part of the bone is removed; unless carefully with suitable instruments to extract.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so that it enlarges with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is no more to remove, then close the wound, if it is wide, and put on one or two ointments suitable for this, to bring out pus, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The clavicle breaks in several places before the shoulder, and the break is in three manners: either it is broken and disjointed into two, with parts, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the aid that feels the broken clavicle; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the break between your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded staff made of cloth or linen, and as thick as needed; and stretch and hold the clavicle, and restrain the staff with your hand, so that you can put the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the clavicle outwards because it comes forward, then it is fitting that the patient lies on their side near their bed, and places a bolster under the shoulder; and have the assistants push the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the clavicle is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find that it is disjointed, it is fitting that you split it apart; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join together with any manipulation, then cut at one of the incisors that you have; but place under the clavicle this instrument, in order to protect the skin.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And make it like a spoon, and do not let it be convex, and let it be as wide as is fitting, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and have two handles, as you see, and let one be broad, and the other narrow, such as is the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured that the wound is hot and suppurating, then wash the wound, and if the scab is small or you doubt whether it is suppurating, then pack the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses with a foul odor come, soak a cloth in oil of roses and lily and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of a bone, when it is in an open wound or cut, is that you apply the plaster made from flour and egg yolk powder, and put on light dressings, and place a splint under the limb, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide band, a palm in width, then put a double cloth over the dressings and plaster; then take a fine splint, three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the splint over the break, and turn the bandage over the healthy joint, and under the diseased one; and clean off the dirt from each part, and as soon as you see that the dressing holds the break correctly, and you see clearly that the splint does not move over the broken bone, so reward it every day, and when the bandages become loose, so restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the person sit with their injured arm over their back, and when they sleep put a small pillow under their armpit to lift it up; this will relieve the strain on the break by aligning the shoulder, or you can tie their arm to their neck, and do not untie it unless something bad happens, for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and keep the splint on until they are restored; and usually they are restored in twenty-eight days, and sometimes even sooner in some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	C'est fini ! Merci pour la traduction de ce texte médiéval sur la réduction d'une fracture d'épaule. Si vous voulez en savoir plus, je peux essayer de traduire un autre texte ou de fournir des informations générales sur le sujet.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	C'est encore un texte médiéval sur la réduction d'une fracture de l'épaule ! Voici ma traduction :
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes in front and points below the skin, then lift up, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the boil to calm the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the swelling (or possibly "the pus")
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The swelling is sometimes broken inside the skin, but it's rare; but it often breaks through to the outside. And when it is broken inside, then it falls down below, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of appetite, and soon, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and it looks very bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and puts .i. cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two collarbones with his hands, and gently places it in every way you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then puts plaster and bandages on top of the thin layer of salt or other light wood, and wraps it up in .i. cloth, and ties it around the broken bone so that it doesn't move; and turns the cord around to the back, and tightens it gradually, and rewards every hour with oil, and if it swells, then tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and clean the plaster, and address what has come there in manners of cures; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Note that the breaking of the ribs does not occur unless they are very large after the back, and at the head within, and only bend forward because they are greasy; and it looks good at the examination on the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put everything back in place the breakage, as it should be. And then put on the plaster, and tighten with a cord, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inclining inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncturing, as well as tears, because the bone pierces the skin; and swells with blisters, vomits a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have applied a great device.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the stomach, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot pustules come, if it has not arrived yet.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they among us said that one applies cupping glasses on the place, in order to draw out thoroughly, and it seems like reason; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass may attract impurities to the place due to weakness of constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they among us said that the place should be covered with damp linen soaked in hot oil, and tents are put between the ribs to make equal heat all around, then it should be treated with the treatment of pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to split open above the place of the fractured rib, and a tool must be placed underneath to protect the flesh; and then one should saw through the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if they are large, and treat him with plasters until he is healed. And if hot pustules come, put wet cloths soaked in rose oil on top of them, and apply them to the place; and cure the place as one should for a pustule, and be careful so that it doesn't become infected, or there will be pain along the costal area where it is until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	It seems like we've finished this passage! The text appears to be a medieval medical treatise on how to treat various injuries and conditions, including fractures and dislocations.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally comes fracture to both bones of the collar, and it occurs when they bend; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and unable to move or stretch, and when you touch them with a needle, it does not feel. Know that they are mortal in many dispositions, and if they can move and feel well when they are strained and touched, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been healed, if one puts treatment on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it has been healed or not, take note if the legs are softened, and if the accident is in the hands, and on the back there is windy weakness and vomiting without will; and when they have vomited on their belly, there is windy weakness and vomiting without will. And when he is tended to on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not work at all in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is much lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is hot swelling, to put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is calmed; then put on one of the soothing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are broken, it is necessary to cover with a poultice; and take out the bone, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam; then cure with ointment dripping grease until he is healed. And if there is a crack in the bone, called the "bone's eye", put your left hand pouch into it and place it equal to the other hand's power, then apply the plaster and the splint if necessary; then bind it tight, and if there are broken bones, make them whole again, take out the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	This appears to be a title or heading in Middle French, which translates to:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, then there will be a slight diminishment to the head; and they become too long, and incline towards the middle, and come to the patient with pain at the place, and swelling, and inflammation of what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand up so high that it reaches the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is at the head alone, then put the same breakage in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is too long, or it inclines towards the inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of this breakage becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put on a splint, then put on a stick of wood or iron, and bind the breakage, so that it does not move; and place the splint under the ribs, until the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and then put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as needed, if there is no bad accident; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The breakage of the arm (or shoulder). This appears to be a medieval medical text discussing various types of injuries and their treatment, specifically fractures and dislocations. The text is written in Old French and includes detailed descriptions of symptoms, treatments, and post-operative care.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The arm (or shoulder) is what lies between the armpit and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways: one being that you take a straight stick of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders together with two strings, and hang them up high, and instruct the patient to sit on one seat; then throw a broken arm over the log so that it comes in line, and place a wooden support in the middle of it, then hang something heavy or have the servants hold it down below; then put the splint level with his hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you strap the patient on their bed, and tie their hand to their neck, then command two servants to have one stretch what is on the splint to his hands, and the other to stretch underneath all of each string, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then strain one string underneath the splint and on top of it, and have each servant extend to its part. And if the splint is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one string in the middle underneath the seat, and the other towards the armpit, underneath the splint; and similarly if the splint is towards the armpit, it is necessary to put one string lightly, without strain, until the splint is even on the arm and on the armpit; then place the splint even as it should be, and strain it, so that a swelling does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a swelling comes, do not strain it for 7 days, and put a warm compress on the splint and in olive oil rose, until the swelling is calmed; then strain it, and the way to strain it is that you put the splint on the arm, then bring the arm up onto the elbow support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put a cloth over it, and strain on the elbow and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is out of place.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not in place, use strapping (steles), and put a thicker and stronger strap on the splint, and space them apart by two fingers, so that each strap is as long as it reaches three finger breadths from each side; then strain on the straps, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the splint, but more strongly and less loose.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the placement of the strapping (esteles) and the tightening, as we have said, to repair the broken member, and you doubt that a hot swelling is coming on, then let it rest in its straps until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each three-day interval to check if there are any signs of irritation or inflammation at the site, or if numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tightly strapped. If so, then do as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accident comes to pass, then do not remove the splint until three days or more have passed, and let the patient sleep on their back with hands on their stomach; and place a pillow filled with wool under the elbow support so that it is even, and observe every hour of the day or night to see if the shape of the broken member is changing, or if the ligatures are becoming looser. If it is healing by virtue of medicine, then give the patient food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is at its first subtlety; and when they begin to recover, let them eat heartily.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones called the "foscile", one small and one large, with the smaller one near the shoulder and the larger one below, towards the elbow. Perhaps the larger bone breaks alone or the smaller one, or perhaps both at once.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the healing is light and easy; but when the large one is broken, the healing is bad and more painful than when both are broken together. If it's just the small bone that's broken, it must be wrapped lightly and put in its place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone that's broken, then it must be straightened more forcefully; and extend it upwards on one cushion, and have the patient's hand held higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and the patient crossed over himself, with a cushion in front of him higher up, so that the patient feels no pain. Then the servants should stretch the patient's arm to the place below their hand, or to one string, and another servant to the other above. And then have the surgeon put it back into its proper form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has caused fragments to be separated, then put each one back in its place. And if there's no loose piece that can be grasped and restored to its place, then do as we said before: operate (or "let an oste" - let a surgeon) on it.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is also an open wound, I have spoken separately about the treatment of that in the chapter on singular cases; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the healing process a blister or abscess forms, take a cloth made of rosin and white wax, not too hard nor too soft, and tie it gently over the blister so that it is calmed. Then remove the wax and apply an ointment made with miller's powder and plenty of egg, and then put on the splints, making sure that the splint for the break is stronger and slightly larger than the others. Know that there should be seven splints or arms in various configurations: whether the break is in one bone or two; and strain more heavily over the break than elsewhere, always pulling less away from it as I said at the beginning of this chapter. And let the cloths on top of the break be soft and moist, not hard or rough, and let the strings that hold them be linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the limb after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, take care to wash the member with hot water until the itching is calmed; and let the member rest not too tightly. And then resume the strapping, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones separated, and it seems like one thing, set it right again.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take note that the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, take care to soften it a little bit, and then let it be for some days until the swelling comes back, and then strain again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have said come to the sick person, then do not untie them until 20 days or thereabouts pass, and then let him put his hands behind his neck, and make sure his necks are equal; and take care to avoid movement and agitation, and sleep on his back. And know that this break is restored in 30 days or 35, or perhaps even 20, depending on the composition and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	It seems we've reached the end of a medical text about bone fractures.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on both thumbs there are small breaks, and it often rains with many drops.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the tip of the hand is broken or swollen, it is necessary that the patient crosses his legs and sits straight in front of him; then he puts his hand on the stretched cloth and stretches the broken bones so they are even with each other as much as possible; and applies an ointment and bandages, if there are swelling, then he wraps a linen sheet according to the quantity of the injury.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the navel of the hand, he makes a sphere with linen and orders the patient to press it against his broken hand; and then binds it with a long sheet, and so that the bandage is as wide as the hand, and it is bound, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the end, it is necessary that you put a bandage on top and another underneath in the hand, so that the fingers are open and straight; then bind the entire hand tightly, and tie the string between the thumbs.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the thumbs, if it's a simple break, tie them even and as necessary; bind the hand with the broken thumb together, and if you see that you put a small straight bandage to lift the break, and don't move it. And if the break is on other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, tie them even and bind them with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all in one hold, which is useful, or place a bandage over it as you would for a boil; and take note of the restoration and arrangement of applying warm compresses, and secure what comes to it, as I said.
