de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons terminé la traduction de ce texte médical ancien. Si vous souhaitez poursuivre avec un autre extrait, n'hésitez pas à le partager !
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	Et c'est là que l'on remarque souvent les fractures de la cuisse, car elles sont fréquentes ; et la guérison s'effectue en attachant une ficelle au-dessus de la fracture, et une autre dessous.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	Et le malade repose sur son lit, puis étend chacun des membres avec une égale tension ; et c'est à ce moment-là que la fracture se produit dans les os.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Et si la fracture est proche de la racine de la cuisse, alors il faut laisser un des liens tendu vers le poignet, et les autres liens à plat sur la fracture. Et ainsi que pour la hanche, où il faudra laisser les liens près de la hanche et l'extension en bas ; puis mettez une attelle ou un étrier en bois autour du membre blessé, avec les deux mains, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit aligné naturellement. Et puis posez un emplâtre et liez-le, si des abcès ne viennent pas.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	Et s'il y a un abcès chaud, laissez-le se cicatriser, puis revenez à votre travail et à votre traitement ; la liaison ou l'attelle est faite de même manière.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	Il convient que vous enveloppiez la fracture d'une banderole en bois doublé en trois ou quatre couches, et que vous laissiez les superfluités, puis tournez la jambe jusqu'à ce que le talon soit à la racine de la hanche ; puis mettez un fil long entre la cuisse et la jambe, près du genou dessous, et laissez les extrémités du fil se terminer au-dessus. Puis tournez sur la jambe et sur la cuisse la banderole, puis mettez des estelles sur la fracture, et une estelle sur l'os de la jambe. Puis emploiez un moule en bois doublé pour maintenir l'étau entre la jambe et la cuisse, afin d'avoir une compression égale ; puis commencez à nouer les trois ou quatre tors en forme d'estelles sur la fracture ; et quant plus vous montez vers la fracture, moins sera l'étirement. Puis tenez ensemble les deux bouts du fil que vous avez mis entre la jambe et la cuisse, et liez les trois estelles qui sont dessus, puis revenez au-dessous jusqu'au bout du fil, jusqu'à ce que vous atteigniez le pied ; et alors l'étau sera serré, si qu'il ne se déplacera pas de sa place. Puis laissez-le ainsi, et s'il n'y a pas d'infection ou d'autre signe semblable, vous avez réussi.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Et si il y a infection, alors déliez l'étau, adressez-vous à ce qui se produit, comme nous l'avons dit maintes fois ; et s'il y a des fragments d'os qui se projettent, il convient de les ramasser, autant qu'on peut.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at any time the skin is broken thus where stars are put in as in an injury and the arm; however, in this restoration made it does not ring out for the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the skin is restored in one day or a little less or a little more according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the shoulder joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the shoulder joint there is little breakage, but it folds many times. And if it breaks, then only it's a slit, or 1 hole, and it has to be all stitched up, and doesn't heal well, and this feels very bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus when you put back in place all that was torn at its joints, as long as it can be assembled; then apply the plaster, and I would put a rounded star on it if needed, and then tighten everything as it should be; then reward all the preparations we have said for other breaks, such as applying heat and similar remedies; and for each accident you put what is necessary until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are 2 bones, of which one is called by right "fibula" and the other is called "tibia"; and it has just as much breakage as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the tibia is broken, then one feels great pain and it can be seen clearly; and turn it downward. Then apply an extension, and put it back together, and tie the stitches equally; however, it is necessary if the break is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be less and lighter; and make it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wooden rods that stretch from one end of the leg to the other, from the knee down to below; then wrap them in two loops with a bandage, one above and one below, and tie it all together in the middle. And at this point, the leg cannot lean to the right or to the left, and thus it is well. Some also provide a splint of the same length as the leg, made of wood, and put the leg in it to hold it steady and properly treat the break or wound. And move each day the leg, to see if there is hot swelling or other accident; and care for it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not often break, but the bones of the foot sometimes do, and you must pay attention, for there is no cure in most cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break, and you see the bones overlapping one another, then put the sick foot on the ground, as if it were going to jump, and then place your other foot on top of it, where the bones are raised, and then press down so that they return to their proper place. Then apply an ointment and bandages, and under the foot of the injured person, a small block with two flat surfaces, and tie it securely to the foot in such a way that the injured part is supported; once you have wrapped everything properly, and done all that you need to do.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, then untie the bandages, for you will find that the bones are back in place, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any toes that are broken, restore them as we have said about the fingers of the hand. Then take a splint for the broken toe and tie it with a string according to its length, making it a little thicker, and then put under the foot the block I mentioned earlier, and secure it firmly in place. And if there are two or three, or more, toes that are broken, then take a separate string for each toe and wrap them together in a piece of linen cloth, and tie the block to the foot securely, so that it is well in place at the head of the block, away from the foot's skin.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things I've said about other breaks, which we've discussed; and provide care for each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the wrist (or forearm)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the wrist (or forearm) is broken in a woman, she should be made to sit with her arm extended, and then inclined towards the back, and supported from behind. Then cotton wool should be packed into the natural cavity, and as much as an egg. After that, the woman should be stood up, and the back should be gently pulled forward, and the cotton wool will spring out, so that it comes to the entrance of the natural cavity, and brings the bone back with it.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the elbow of the man is broken, or that of the woman, restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hand; and these near fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into them and attends to my book. For a fracture signifies more than one disposition for the right way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's girth and put the penis into it; then bind it with cloth around, and let it be so for three days or longer, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with an open wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a fracture with an open wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the thigh or the armpit or similar, that he be sutured now, so that the sutures which we have mentioned may bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the bone remains brittle from vitriol, then if you have no other choice, start to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, before a swelling comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a swelling comes, then leave the restoration just until the fifth day, so that the swelling is calmed down, and don't touch it for another third or quarter of a day, because you would bring on a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed above the skin and visible, it's necessary that you cover it with a light dressing in your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	Et se li extensions ne t'est apparillie pour mettre egal a tes mains, si leve le ramoingne avec cet instrument qui est de fer, qui a 7 doigts ou 8 de long, et la largeur est selon la quantité de la plaie. Et pour cela est nécessaire au maire qu'il emprunte 3 ou 4, selon ce qu'il en a besoin en chacune cure de fracture; et soit rond et un peu gros, qui ne plie mie à la compression sur le membre à ton ouvrage, et soit aiguisé devant, et grossi du milieu en avant, ainsi:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved nails should be placed on the head of the visible bone; and you press down once, as long as it yields, and they are equal to each other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, then use a suitable instrument, such as a chisel or saw, at your disposal; then remove what remains in the bone from sharpness and small scabs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned to its place, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural location. So do this until it is in its place, then moisten one cloth in black vinegar, and properly sew it up; and do not put cerote or other ointment on the wound if it has oil, lest you cause putrefaction and corruption to come; then administer remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the bandage all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the break; and many times they have done this foolishly, and caused death or corruption to come on the patient sometimes; and the straining is softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that some bad accident may come to it, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, then do not put on salves; but envelop it around with hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two hours a bowing to the wound, then remove what you have put on it all together, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacical ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the bandage on the member two times a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is bound and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the bowing goes downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it has been many days and cannot heal but rather keeps bowing, know that there are small bones inside, which is why you should seek the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose bone fragments that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or other sign of corruption comes to the place, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the shinbone or the ulna, and similar ones of the large limbs, do not extract it, for many times gangrene ensues, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The swellings that come on the sore. (This appears to be a quote from a medieval medical text, possibly related to the treatment of wounds or injuries.)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We see many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the swelling is fresh: administer purgative medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, either separately or together, and mix them with a purging wine or with egg whites or with vinegar; and apply them to the sore in poultices, and strain it well, and do not loosen it for a day; then loosen it and repeat another one, until the swelling is gone; or you may apply it on a well-made piece of cloth; for the property of cloth is that it removes all the swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut off the excess, or have it cut by a surgeon, until it is gone, and cure the wound as long as it remains healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which is weak after recovery. (This phrase suggests that the text may be discussing the treatment or care of a patient who has experienced physical weakness or debilitation after recovering from an illness or injury.)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is healed and there remains after the member weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not as tight as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to a multitude of swelling; or due to excessive movement, neither in its right time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great nourishment, and washes it often with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the member twisted after healing. (This phrase suggests that the text may be discussing the treatment or care of a patient who has experienced physical deformity or twisting of a limb after recovering from an injury or illness.)
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, although its natural function is not lost: do not believe the foolish people who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great evils, and perhaps death. However, if the nodules and tortures are fresh, it is necessary to remove them with warm water, or herbs that soften, such as mullein leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the musilage of mullein, mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top. Or take fatty figs, grind them with coltsfoot seeds, and similar medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at all times remove the nodule by continued and long rubbing with wet hands, and administer movement to the member every hour. (This suggests that physical therapy or manipulation of the affected area may be an effective treatment for this condition.)
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened and turned into stone-like hardness, and it needs to be removed with a knife, then cut just up to the bone, carefully and lightly with a sharp razor. And cover with a compress and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here starts the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it must be returned to its proper place immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one waits, the swelling will increase, and by chance if one sets it back in place while it is swollen, then it should not be moved until it has subsided: for it can bring forth spasms and other pains, many times.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, one makes the patient better, then leaves it alone until the swelling has subsided; then one raises the limb with hot water and oil, then gently cleanses it, and cures each member as the cure comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have outlined the chapters on dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	What happens when the jaws are dislocated and they hang down, and the dislocation of both is in two manners: either they are slightly out of their place and softened a bit; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva from the mouth drips and it cannot hold its mouth closed, nor can it enclose its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to place on its own within a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you should clean it immediately, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendants grasp the patient's head, and press the mirror or spoon pouch from one of their hands into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands are outside to keep it equal; and command the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts the mirror or spoon pouch into place until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw does not return easily, even if it is both jaws together, then one raises them with hot water and oil, until they are cleaned lightly; nor delay in returning the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned to their proper position and the patient's mouth is closed well without being too soft, then one puts a damp cloth on it in the shape of a circle made from rose oil and wax, and ties it lightly with moist thread.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on their back and their jaws are placed between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor do they struggle to chew, but rather take light food until the pains are gone and the jawbones have been quieted.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then take what they want lightly, and do not strain themselves to open their mouth while eating and drinking, as long as the jaw is well quieted and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then it comes to fever and severe pains, and possibly a diarrhea, and perhaps a vomiting of cold pure liquid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a bad sign; and many times death comes to the person in whom this occurs within 8 days.
de la forcelle	the dislocation of the jaw (from the previous text)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot descend from the cheekbone to the jawbone and is easily felt when it occurs.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back and stretches out their arms; then they press the cheekbone firmly against one's palm, and it will return to place; afterwards, apply a poultice and bandage, and restrain it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the jaw that is near the cheek cannot dislocate; but if it does, and you clean it and put it back in its place as we have said, then apply a poultice and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly, the jaw is brought back into place when it becomes dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder can become dislocated in three ways: first, it can become dislocated below the armrest; second, it can become dislocated towards the front of the body (shoulder blade); and third, although rare, it can become dislocated upwards.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not become dislocated backwards or inwards towards the nerves; but rather, it often becomes dislocated downwards towards the armrest, and this is especially true for those who are thin, as their shoulder blade jumps out easily; whereas for those with enough flesh, it will pop out to a point and then return to its place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens that some men have a blow or bruise, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you should examine it carefully until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is clear that a dislocation occurs when it [the shoulder] goes down towards the armrest, and you can distinguish between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder and below the armrest at the elbow, in the shape of an empty space, just as if it were a bird's nest; and the patient is unable to bring their hand back to their chest or make any movements with it.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you can clearly see the deformity at the elbow.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not easily reducible, whether it is new or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician lifts the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the armrest, and forces the joint back to its place with great force; and the physician lifts the hand and stretches it upwards, then places it down again, and it will come into place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come into place within the time we have said, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the physician should apply soothing and calming ointments, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and bring them to the affected area.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	And then the patient should be placed on their back and a cloth of linen of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armrest; then the physician should place their foot on top of the cloth, and with a firm but gentle motion, lift the head of the shoulder and pull the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another physician should tie the patient's head so that it does not move down; with this, the shoulder will return to its place immediately. And if you see that it comes back in this manner, then you know that the dislocation is corrected.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and you should have a man who is larger than the patient present, and he should stand with his back to the side of the patient, and push his shoulder under the armrest of the patient, and lift the armrest up, so that the patient's body hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another physician should pull the patient's hand downwards towards their stomach. And if the patient is too light, then you can hold something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return to its place immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the reduction is also done in another way: and it consists of placing a long wooden skewer into the ground, where the jawbone is as wide as a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and it is placed under the patient, so that it is draped softly above them, and the patient holds the long handle of the skewer; then their hand is stretched downwards from the other side in a firm manner, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return by all the means we have said, then make this treatment: take a stick of two arms' breadth and four thumbs' width in diameter, with its end rounded so that it can easily enter into depth under the armrest, in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then take the rope from above the beam and wrap it around the arm so that the arm is not injured; then place the patient's elbow under the arm; stretch his arm over the long beam, and tie the shoulder to the beam, and his hand at the tip of the hand, then put the arm on one shelf of a wooden splint wide enough, and have him stretch out his hands down, and let his body hang from the other side: the joint will be restored now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that you place under the arm a wooden staff of wool equal to it, then put the poultice around the powder from the mill with incense and onion broth over the entire shoulder and around, then apply the straining cloth under the arm carefully, and turn the string on the poultice, and encircle the hand around his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he drink broth until the limbs are comforted, because he will heal more quickly; and then drink more after five days or seven, and move him; and if it is firm and has not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen because of too much moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizers to three small holes, as long as it is placed in front of the cauterizer's cauldron.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it does not heal after seven days, and the joint does not hold together and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the chest or shoulders, or back, is caused by a blow and stretching of the hands, and it should be treated in another manner; and it cures as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes pain and stiffness in the member, and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until the pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	De la dislocation du coude ! (Il y a une marque d'exclamation qui manquait dans le texte original)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and especially before and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, for one sees it clearly and feels it clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the diseased shoulder with the healthy one, it cannot be seen clearly. For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you treat it before the swelling comes, for if the swelling comes, it would be hard to reduce it; and perhaps it cannot be reduced completely at all, especially when it is behind; and it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the treatment is this, when it can be reduced to such a state that you can reduce it, that you stretch out his hand to your two hands; and his arm be spread wide, and the hands of the examiner according to the shoulder around, above and below, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, as long as it revives to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and puts pressure on the root of the palm on the joint that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and let two attendants extend the arm, and both bind it, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then wrap a long and wide double cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the surgeon joins the joint to his hand, he rubs it with oil to soften the joint, then pushes the joint firmly until it comes back.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is back in place, he puts on dry plaster with plenty of egg white, and strains it firmly, and suspends the arm to the patient's neck, and leaves it for some days, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, he releases the bandage and leaves it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, he re-applies the plaster and the bandage, and leaves it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then he releases it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain or swelling after the reduction of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, he bathes and rubs it gently, and presses until it is eased; or he puts a fatty lamb's snow on the joint, then leaves it for one day and one night, then removes it, and lets him enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, he gently rubs the joint, then puts the snow on it again, and then enters the bath; and thus does this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see that the joint still hurts, he puts on warm wetened flax with butter, and presses it on; it will return to its normal state.

Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. And the reduction is that you place the patient's hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of their hand, and the practitioner places it even, so that they put their palm over the appearance of the joint, and press it until it comes back to its place.

de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder joints

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the vertebrae of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are several that are dislocated, then there is no remedy, for the bone hastens to kill the sick person.

Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the vertebrae move to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gyphosis".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure is that you reward it if the gyphosis came from childhood: there is no cure or healing of the whole thing if not.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old people said it was a manner of cure by great words, but there is no great benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.

et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and in each splint there is one hole, where the turntable runs, and the splints are firmly planted in the ground so they do not move; and between each two splints there is another turning splint, on which the turntable turns, and in both turning splints there are two small splints of an inch in length to turn the turntable.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the thread that is among the splints to the turntable towards the head, and the other thread towards the feet to the other turntable; and each of the servants turns their turntable so that all the thread is wound up, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is evened out, he puts on desiccating poultice with an abundance of egg, and then the pads, and then the splint of a wooden board three fingers long, which should prop up the place of the gilboseity and the part of the spine that is sound, then tie it with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient in gentle nourishment until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if any problem comes in the end of healing, it is necessary to administer soothing and softening medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and at no time give more than one piece of poultice.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and whenever there appears a deformation in the back part of the spine of the back, and one thinks it might be a displacement; and it is the bone that protrudes, therefore we should not have any presumption: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Displacements of the shoulder joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that the joints of the shoulder and the joints of the arm do not come out without dislocations only, nor does it happen as with other joints; and the joint of the shoulder is displaced in four ways: inward and outward, and forward and backward; and more inward thus, and less outward forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when you put the sick leg together with the healthy one, it is longer, and shows more swelling in the sick knee than in the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place where there is a warm swelling of an aposteme because the veins of the thigh come to that place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes outwards is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose it comes forward are that his leg feels well in accordance with its completion; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, holds back his urine, swells the groin, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose it comes behind are that he cannot straighten his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the level of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you should return to see if the dislocation is old and has remained in its position, and there is no cure; and one must not have presumptions.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four manners of dislocation, hasten to turn back the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and bend it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare one strong person, and stretch the leg very much with both hands, or with one strap tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another person stretches his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then he tightens it with one strap over the knee; and another ties the end of the strap.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch up and down all at once, until the sick person is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to three signs, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If this is not so, then you must apply treatment to its sign. When the dislocation is at breaking point, it is necessary that you place the sick person on his healthy side, then put the strap above the root of the knee, and the part that is under the ankle, then stretch the strap up towards the ankle, and towards the thigh.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another person's arms and encircle the thick part of the sick knee, and stretch it out to the outside strongly: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot squeeze it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong and soft strap from one to the other above the two heels, and above the two knees, and that the sick leg be stretched two fingers more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then it should be hung from the top of a beam and be above the ground two arms' length; then command one servant to encircle the head of the knee, and another servant hanging with the sick person, who tightly encircles the knee, for the joint comes back quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at its limit, then place the sick person on their back, as we have said in the one with a hip deformity, and tightly stretch one strap above the healthy leg, and also above the pelvis.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert one of the torches between the knees of the sick person in the middle, forming a kind of... (wait, I think I see where this is going) ...a primitive splint?
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have damp cloths planted around him so that he doesn't hurt himself, then stretch each servant towards him, and the physician places his hand on the patient's hand where the dislocation is.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, put him on the table and press him in this way as we have said in the cubbing, and place the patient on his left side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be stretched out quickly, and as I said; and place the mirror so that it hurts the patient's skin over the knee joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the elbow.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it should not be stretched out downwards or lifted up on the ground, but rather that it should be in the same way as if the hip was displaced to the back, just as we have said about lying on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and it should be on its face, and the ligament stretched as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be in place when the patient stretches their legs and they are equal; then bring together the thighs, and put a pad and strap made of cloth on them, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and if it rests for 3 or 4 days, then untie and put the pad on top; and if you see that they are equal, leave the strap as before, for 3 days, then untie and make it walk gently, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	It seems we've reached the end of this medical text's section on joint dislocations.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward, outward, and behind; and do not come out in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at their knee and if it does not straighten out at their knee, know that they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit upright and stretch out their leg if they can, and place your back on their chest and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee with your palms and draw it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee together, and another assistant stretches out their foot, so that the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that they straighten out their leg slightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the plaster on it and make them stretch out their leg to their knee and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it, and do not have the patient walk until the member is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the member does not improve, have them stretch it strongly, as we said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like we've moved on to a new topic.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of this are that the ankle is inflamed, and tense before the part where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return to its place is light, and one should extend it lightly with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, it is advisable that you make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly with one hand, i.e. grasp him above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and put the foot firmly in place upstairs;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice more, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back into place, that is well; if not, then repeat the work, for it will come back.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot come back in place like this, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place one strap firmly on the ground between his thighs, and tie it tightly around, so that it does not harm the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then grasp the strap and pull it down to one hand or a rope, so that they can tie it above the ankle.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch out each strap equally, and the straps should be put between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when one is pulling.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then put the fingers of each person with their hands in the same position as the dislocation, and have another person grasp the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, then put on the plaster and bandage above, and shape the splint, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the straps are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then leave it for two or three days, and if the straps loosen, then re-tie them. Then untie him on the third day or a quarter, and forbid the patient to go about for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes out before this time is up, it's not certain that it will not still come loose again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the swelling, you should drain it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	It looks like this text may be coming to an end! "Des dois" means something like "to the hands" or "as for what remains", but in this context, it's likely just a concluding phrase indicating that the instructions are finished. Is there anything else you'd like me to help with?
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulder is no longer swollen, it should be well-stretched without effort, and that's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on one flat place or on one table entirely straight, and put your foot on what is seen of these joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is equalized, and nothing appears, you put under the sole of the foot a table at two stools, then strain strongly, and let him be for three days, then loosen him, and have him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it has happened that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, since you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor too hasty;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning soothing applications and poultices warm, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then clean the member now thoroughly, so that the warm poultice comes on it;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is clean, then administer soothing applications and warm poultices, and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is fracture, and small bones are splintered, then set them, and do as we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and be careful not to go down the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is worth more to you than your Creator, and for the sake of your soul and body's salvation. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The explicit rule of medicine
